O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine, its fulfillment, and have concluded it with explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I completed this with a treatise, which is the part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is closely guarded in our region and unknown throughout, the science has degenerated and become depleted, and there remains no trace of its power other than small descriptions in ancient books about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and knowledge is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive this treatise by ordering it according to the method of exposure and description and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of cautery instruments and other tools used in the work with the addition of descriptions and preparations for their use, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are to be found in our time, the art of medicine has become neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wishes to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, must know the judgment of the members, their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of their openings, and understand the movement and rest of veins, and from where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that ignorance is death, and knowledge is life; especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, risks being led astray and mistreating people; as I have often seen happen to many who engage in this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a most strange sight, where an abscess on the scrotum or neck of a woman burst, and the arteries in her neck flowed; so much blood came out that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another sight where a stone was extracted from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; it took away a piece of his bladder, and he bled internally for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; I knew well that if it was not cut out, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another marvel that took place in the care of our duke who had broken a leg and suffered a wound from the fracture; all the ignorant healers held the fracture over the wound as if it were a strong hold, leaving no trace of healing to the wound, and they left it like that until the end; and they commanded him not to dislocate it; and he waited until the leg was completely swollen and gangrenous and came to a bad end.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	They called me to come to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I heard it dislocate, it was as if it were at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corruption was already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I also saw another wonder: the abscess became worse, and then it was inflamed due to the malignancy of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it does not suit that one should touch it with iron if it is not in a part that can be entirely removed what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear child, it is necessary that you know that the art of healing is divided into two parts: that is to say, the work of hands where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show you in each part of this book where there is fear and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, hold yourself in such a way that the evil eye cannot speak ill of you. If you take up your weapons courageously and gently, and embark on your sick with resolve, using the best means so that by the grace of God you may be saved and rejoice; cast away diseases fraught with sorrow, disarm those things that make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in none of his warnings: "Do not take any sick condition too seriously, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cautery and medical agues, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; and includes the forms of instruments, the tools for cautery, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it includes the ordering and forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions; it ordains the use of the hands and shapes of instruments from the wrist to the foot.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So, remembering the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of aid and the harm or benefit of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and their harm are the longest and most subtle knowledge, revealing secrets; on this topic, many sages have spoken and agreed, and I will leave it at that, as I fear to prolong my words.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for every complexion where it has matter, whether the complexities: that is to say, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In both hot and dry complexions, matter is present, and some people devise that cautery is great help, while others say the opposite: that cautery is useless for illnesses arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat for hot illnesses, nor by dryness; and he who says the contrary states that cautery provides great help to hot and dry diseases that come upon the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the heat of fire, you feel the body is warm.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should attempt it unless they have tried it themselves, and know by long experience the chapter of cautery, and the diversity of human dispositions, and the causes of their illnesses, and the remedies and the time of day; for other dispositions we only have fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and came together for the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, son, that cautery combines fire in a way that is a secret of healing, and indeed it is a greater kindness than the fiery medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from outside except to the member that is hot, and it does not harm any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fiery medicines pass from one member to another by distance, and they bring to the member diseases of sorrow that have no cure; and sometimes the fire causes the patient pain because of its high intensity and the goodness of its substance, unless there is an excess of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And if you have found me through experience and the long service and study that I have put into this art, and it is in accordance with the truth of things; and because I excuse myself for the length of my words, as I do not wish to reveal the secret hidden within fire, and the quality of the work, how it heals the ailments of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know this, my son, that there is agreement among them as to when cauterization should be performed and the prayers recited.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the pain causing harm is removed with the help of cauterization; and most importantly, cautery is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do who follow folly; for to the illness that is healed by cautery there is no return; and thus it should be. But they are mistaken, because cautery is not a cure that changes the constitution, dries up humors that cause pain, and is effective only for the urgency of its value and the virtue of its work and mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another thing to consider is that illness comes in various forms according to the constitution of the patient and the place where it arises, and its power; and impurities gather within it through the acquisition of foods and similar things. But if cautery is administered when there is a lack of impurities and moisture—as with the cautery for pain and similar conditions—this type of pain does not return, but rather occurs rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine; it's clear. But they do not believe that cautery has any value after medicine, as when we administer methods of treatment for any illness and they are ineffective, then we should resort to cautery, and it does have value.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is indeed the last resort of medicine, not at all according to the understanding of learned fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are more effective than iron ones, and they only spoke of fire for the quality of gold and for the excellence of its substance; they said that the heat of cautery does not cause blisters, but this is not certain, as I have tested it, and I have found that it is true in no one; and gold cautery is more effective than iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat the gold instrument, you are not sure if it is heated by the color of the gold, and as soon as it cools down; and if it is heated too much, it becomes damaged; thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery as we have equipped it with our tools for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now we have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the way may be lighter to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery is useful for moisture and cold on the head, and it helps with conditions caused by a disease called "soda," and by many humors that flow from the head to the ears, and due to numerous dreams and toothaches and throat pain, and especially with all diseases caused by cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purified by a solvent medicine, cleansing the head three times or four, according to the virtue and age and usual condition of the patient, and then make the head dry again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make it rest crossed in your hands, and place his hands on some weight; after, put the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his two fingers; and let it be where your two middle fingers meet, if it bleeds, then heat the cautery called "olive," which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And mark it on the skin with ink, then gently lower and stretch your hand slowly, dislocating it; afterward, lift your hand carefully, and reset the joint when you see the bone is slightly out of place; if you do not see it, repeat the cautery process until you do. Then take a small piece of rope, put soft, melted butter and cotton inside, place it on the joint, and leave it for three days; afterward, cover it with moistened cotton, leaving it until the burn from the heat is healed; finally, treat the wound with 'tetrafarmacon' ointment while it remains clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say that the older a wound is, the more it purifies itself; and for this reason, aid must be moved quickly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must not leave the cautery for so long that the bone itself is burned; then remove the burned part from the bone, and it will be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another says that one must not leave the cautery for so long, and push with such force to remove the bone as wide as a woman opens her legs to let humors out; one should keep the wound open for a long time; then one must clean it and dress it properly.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in all cases, except for those in which any man has no choice but despair; and I think I should leave it. For the joint is weakened by continuous dissolution of nature, as we witness in other members; and also when the patient's joint is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization seems safer and more mobile to me, and from this I use them together for the greater good.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes on and lasts for a long time, patients must use herbal remedies and pills known as "cough drops", and applications of poultices; and if one undergoes the cauterization that we have mentioned above, it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's limb is of strong nature and not too stiff; then cauterize it from below, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each horn of the skull up to the bone, as we have said before, and cauterizing the one called "vasselz" (the vessel), which is where the ventosas are placed, hold your hand slightly away so that you do not see the bone. The patient feels much greater pain from this cauterization than from others, and I will speak of it then; it is necessary that the cauterization of the horns be more precise than that of the middle part of the skull, and this is its form.
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head there is sudden pain, and the disease extends to the oil (or perhaps meaning 'body') up to the very last moment, and the seeds are expelled by means of medicated drugs, and all other cures as I have mentioned in the division of diseases, prove ineffective; then one should perform cauterization according to two methods, that is, with hot ague medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with hot ague medicine involves pricking a dose of alder (or possibly another herb) and removing the bark and covering it with wax in such a way that you can replace the alder beneath the skin; hold it there tightly for twelve hours, then release it and treat the wound vigorously with hot compresses for two or three days, then apply clean cotton soaked in butter until the discharge ceases.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment as long as it is healed; and if you see fit to use any burning medicines that I have written about or dosed in the treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this tool:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "close" because the head is shaped like a circle with a small depression, and in the middle there is a slight appearance; place it on the painful limb, hold your hand, and gently turn it slightly until half of the thickness of the heart is burned; then remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is dangerous, and abundant blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton in the wound and keeping it there for three days, then he moistens the cotton with butter and continues to treat the wound until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called 'cultellare' (scalpel), be careful not to cut into the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When treating migraine as we have previously discussed in divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit from the cautery that medicine recommends, then you must heat the cautery called 'cultellare' (scalpel) until it is bright white; and then make a sign on the suffering limb with a line half an inch long, pull your hand away once, so as not to cut into the artery and do not let blood come to the bone; and be careful of the lower jaw when chewing, so that the teeth do not move and spasms do not come to the patient, and beware of the flow of blood from the artery when it is cut, or great fear will come especially to those who do not know how, and who are not well-versed and experienced; and leave the work half-finished. But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery is not enough to heal the disease, and the patient suffers, apply it again to the main part as we have said, and cure the wound while it is still healthy; and if you notice, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on extracting an artery, with a cautery having two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful than the others.

After having marked around the painful ear, or both ears if they hurt on one side and the other, and moved it slightly away from the root of the ear after having signified the joint's position, place 10 points around each ear; then treat the joint until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	regarding the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture that requires cautery is limited to those that involve fluid movement, as we have mentioned in the divisions of illness; and do not perform cautery on parts that are merely dry, sore, or swollen.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of pain that mutates from fluid of water and purging from the head and gargarism, and it doesn't improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three types of cautery: one at the root of the ear, another slightly away from the temple, and the third in the adjustment of the two lips; and place the cautery on the area that opens to a healthy part, burning half of the heart's base, and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the surgical knife we have described before, but this one is a bit more subtle, and the blade should be slightly thicker; after curing it, as I have said above, as long as it remains healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not benefit the patient, and they do not have a fever, then make four cauterizations: two on the temples at the back of the head, one on the forehead, and one on the liver, which is called "vessel" as we have previously mentioned, and no cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	The term "de litargie" seems to be a

de la froidor dou chief	from cold at the top

After removing the head of the patient, make the dislocation well-made, as round as a circle, and place it back on the head; let the patient lie with their eyes crossed and well held from all sides; then apply the liniment, and rub with butter of old nettles; heat it over fire temperately, so that the patient can bear it; afterward empty the circle inside the head and leave it to cool; and repeat this to the patient once a week with another good treatment until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you must cauterize it, make many points at the cautery.

de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes

dou poil qui point l’oil	the hairs that prevent the oil from entering

No time does it happen that the hairs of the skin turn white and prickle, and they point towards the flesh; and cauterization is performed in two ways: namely, with fire or with hot medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent. The medicinal cautery of burning herbs is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a parchment shape of the leaf of mirth. And know that the ability of men is diverse in size and strength, and according to your constraints; and do not turn away from the right path those who have study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have discussed regarding diseases, and your treatments do not benefit the patient, then it is necessary to perform cautery on them in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head on a healthy surface, and hold their neck between your hands in this manner so that their head does not move, nor do they remove their head from your grip. Afterwards, apply moist cotton or persil juice over the oil. Then, heat the cautery tool until it is hot, making sure its shape resembles a quill, with the end being the cautery point. If you see fit, the point can be angled downwards or upwards, and if not, it should resemble a tent. However, any position that ensures stability during your work is preferred.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it and drain the pus and fluid; if it is closed again, work on it and extract the bowels; then apply hot cautery, holding your hand over the cautery at the affected area above the oil, so that your hand does not cause damage; place the cautery on the fat of the oil and burn.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you begin the cautery near the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not work, repeat the cautery again, and if necessary, a third time, leaving it for three days; then apply moistened butter cotton and cure the dry dressing until it is healed, and if forty days pass without healing, apply a corrosive medicine as needed, depending on what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a kind of cautery for a fistula that no one of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and fix its position; then place a fine, sharp instrument into the gap, by which the shape is formed.
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it should have the quantity of a drop of water; and hold your hand firmly, so that the patient does not move at all, until the pus has drained completely to its core; and one should put cotton moistened with oil on top of the wound for healing or in order to stop the flow: the pus will be gently pulled from the fistula, and health will return miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the ulcer is clean through the cautery we have mentioned, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to administer ice or cold water, and return the ulcer to the body within the cold, according to what is appropriate for its place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks appear in the lips, which are called "poil," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds as we have discussed in detail, and the treatment does not benefit, then use a small cauterizing instrument according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place the instrument in these wounds until it reaches the bottom; then treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the mouth
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the root of the mouth or in the uvula or palate or at the roots of the teeth, causing putrefaction and rot and becoming a fistula, then treat it as we have discussed in detail; however, this treatment does not benefit. In such cases, you should perform cauterization according to the size of the fistula. After emptying or opening the fistula, hold your hand firmly until the heat from the cautery reaches the bottom, and do this once or twice, following up with treatment as we have described in detail, until it is healed; and if it heals in this way, that is good. If not, it is necessary to expose the area and remove the corrupt bone, as you will find specified in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	no movement of the joints
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and treatment with medicine is ineffective, then place the patient's aching jaw in a healthy position; afterwards, heat the cautery instrument according to the shape that comes, as if you put a cane on the tooth; and apply the hot cautery to the root of the tooth firmly, holding your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the tooth's root; then release your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your will; afterwards, make the patient rinse his mouth with salty water, and do this for an hour and a half strong.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this same manner, the tooth that was moving becomes confirmed, the gums are softened and restrained, and the moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	about the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold, or there is frost or chill, and the remedies of medicine are ineffective, then it needs cauterization according to these two methods: the butter cauterization and the fire cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	The butter cauterization is such that you press melted butter into a copper or iron spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a stick, dip it in the melted butter, and apply it to the aching tooth until it cools; do this often enough so that its effect reaches the root of the tooth. If you see that the butter and cotton are too dry, apply it again to the aching tooth, and hold the hot iron until the heat rises up the side of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	He uses fire cautery, making it as hot as you can bear a metal pin or arrowhead, so the flames do not reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, from which its shape will come, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be alleviated that very day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is important that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of this cautery, and then sucks on a hot cloth; and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And do cautery on the upper lip where you wish, according to what you can do; and this is the shape of the pin.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is from cold moisture and does not respond to medication, then heat the cautery head with this after which the shape should appear, and it should have openings for the smoke to escape from the cautery of the other part; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or as needed until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply cautery according to its quantity, leaving it for three days; then cover with moist cotton and butter until the burning is removed; afterwards treat the wound with oil and bandages until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture conquers the channels of the body, especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should be relieved first with solvent medicines; after that, make them cough up at the root of the throat, and be sure not to go down to the throat, and only cough gently.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, make another cautery at the joint of the collarbone and the top of the spine, and these cauteries that are called "claws" from which we have the form above; and treat the limb as we have said above until it is healed.
de la toust	from the heat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and any disease of the muscles is due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or inflammation, and it is an old illness, then make two cauterizations on the strong parts of their own will; and another cauterization between the two breasts; and this cauterization which is called 'clavile' according to the shape mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a cauterization by pricking all the cauterization called 'poins' from which the shape is as mentioned above in the illness of the ears; and the points can be up to 30, or more inside.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment, reset it according to what is said above, and make the cauterization in three parts according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cautery is lighter, because you do it three times in turn.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	On the dislocation of the shoulder.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, remember to have the patient recall their pain on their back and side. Afterwards, gently apply pressure with your left hand to the area where the dislocation is located; if the joint is misaligned inside, heat the cautery with two thin irons until it forms this shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and burn the heart as long as it feels burning, and make the shape of the burn with four burns, and for this reason, the burn is made with a burn tool having three prongs, so that the burn shapes are six burns; and the nerve is according to the subtlety of a thread, and this is the form of the burn with three prongs.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never should it be adjusted on this nerve, for there are eight burns.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the burn, put a cloth made of silk over it; then rest the patient, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, such a thing happens poorly, then make a fire cautery on the thick skin with a cautery claw or many cauteries with sharp points.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed, and health returns to the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach while it is being stretched from its natural state, catarrh multiplies within it, and conventional treatment methods do not help, then the patient should be careful on his back, extending his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From this and afterward, make three cauterizations and remove the knife with the least amount of a finger's width, cauterizing all the way to the bone; and two cauterizations should be made on each side until the shape of the cauterization is at three angles, and there is enough space between them that they are not joined together while they rot; and make the cauterization so complete that it sears both parts of the heart, and the shape of the cauterization remains unaltered.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you are to be cauterized with a large cautery on the stomach according to this form, and he who is afraid of this cautery, make a single point with the cautery and sign on the stomach according to the amount that you see fit; then cauterize all the way through the cautery called "point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have previously discussed, as long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver experiences pain from cold and moisture and excessive flatulence, as long as it is out of its natural state due to superfluities; and the patient is treated according to what we have mentioned in sections, but it does not help, then it is necessary that the patient be mindful of his head. And a sign of three cauterizations following this form and figure and quantity on the liver, to remove the humors, should be performed; and there should be enough space between each cauterization, approximately the thickness of a finger; and the cauterization should be long across the body, without pressing too hard with the hand on the entire cauterization; and it should only burn the middle part of the heart, and the patient should be straight on his feet; if he cannot, he should lie down, extend his legs, and ease his breath. And this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish, cauterize these wounds with a cuttlefish knife, if you are skilled and sharp in the art, and be careful not to burn yourself entirely, for you would scorch the whole body; and that it does not come to a boil, because the blood vessels there are very delicate, and only the wise will see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you need to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels moderate pain; but if it is in the membrane, they feel intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure requires a mirror, the patient must rest their head; then clean the wound where the abscess is, and apply the hot cautery which resembles a rose, in this way:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cautery until the veins are burned, and come close together, as long as the pus is completely drained; after treatment, follow it up with cleansing until it is healed; and it is not advisable to use this cautery unless by one who has studied medicine for a long time and knows how these ailments can be worsened.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can safely operate, but I still think it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Fire cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	They say that one should make cautery on the pleura with roots of aristologe, in this way: take a long root of aristologe, the largest you can find, dry and as thick and as long as your arm; moisten it in oil, heat it over fire, and cauterize between the ribcage and collarbone, and make smaller cautery descending into the area beneath the beard; and cauterize between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly sloping behind; and one cautery across the anus, and another on the stomach, and between the shoulders, and along both sides of the lower ribs, removing the cautery between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but hold it open as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say that no old man should use fire cautery like a razor, scorching it and placing it between the ribs, until it reaches that abscess; and there is great pain, as we have said about the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this case, there is great fear among the patients, and many die now, or a fistula appears that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said about the divisions of treatments, and it does not benefit, then they attach three ways of cautery that are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Dislocate the joint in such a way that you make three cauterizations, or four, according to the length of the bone, and the figure of the cautery we have mentioned before; do not press your hand too hard on the cautery, and let the patient be cautious on his back. Another method of cauterization is to heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; ease the pain that is in the bone where you remove the cautery, or the patient's complaint comes from the left side, and raise up accordingly to the pain, according to the length of the body, and make the cauterization according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After you have withdrawn the two nerves, inflame them until the bone is felt on the other side, then quickly remove the cautery, and thus you will have four. And if you see that the cauterization is not complete at three nerves, continue to cauterize at three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After treatment when the pus has drained for a long time, this is more effective than any of the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	The term "ydropisie" is the Old French form
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not effective against hydrops, except in the manner known as "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	If your treatment according to the methods we have discussed in sections does not help, then you should make four cauterizations around the wound, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in the anus; and the cauterizations should be close to the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open for a long time to allow pus to drain, and not letting the treatment of the sick person continue after the cautery, healing would be hastened, and the two cuts would heal together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the abdomen is the nail that we have shown before, and for the back it is olive-shaped, according to what has been placed before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the stones
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the stones are swollen in a person who is jaundiced and filled with dark urine, you should cauterize just below the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and gently hold your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not press too deeply, so as to close the natural opening; thus the heat from the fire will penetrate the flesh according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two fires on each leg, one at the tip of the cutaneous edge, and the other opposite, near the knee; leave the fires to grow long without healing, allowing the skin to heal; then perform the other treatments we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the wound
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When abdominal pain arises from cold and moisture, the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any means; you see the patient suffering greatly with intense pain, so perform a large fire on the stomach according to what has been said before about the stomach fire, or a fire around the navel with subtle fires placed at every cautery, and two fires on the haunches.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make a burn on the finger, and a burn on every part, and small burns on the gentle stomach, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	**On the Treatment of Hemorrhoids**
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are at the root, or in one or more places, and they have been long-standing and are composed of corrupt cold and moist humors, they are treated as we have said in divisions, but these cauterizations do not help: On the spine of the back, that which is entirely deprived of warmth, gently apply and gradually in a triangular pattern; one cauterization below the buttocks two times; and if you think his stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and bloating is seen on the face, then apply a strong cauterization on the stomach as has been said before, and another on the liver, and yet another on the heart at all cauterizations; and leave the cauterization open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, reset the shoulder as long as it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	from the fleshiness called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you deal with the fleshiness (thelul), if the cautery appears too sharp, then take a hot iron and burn it into that flesh; leave it in place until the cautery has healed, from which the wound will close; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each area as we have said; after the beneficial treatment of ointments, as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large iron on the chest (alchatim), it will provide greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	From the poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or incising, which we will describe in its place, such a disease comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When no vein becomes fistulated, and there is swelling, putrefaction, and corrupt moisture, you must try all sorts of subtle remedies, and be sure to know at every stage how effective they are.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease

de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the back (or "hainche" as written)

When pain arises in the back (or "hainche") due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured through the methods we have described, but the cure is ineffective, and the illness persists, then it is necessary to purge the patient of foul humors with either bad-smelling pills or other similar good pills.

Never should cautery be performed in the middle on top of the collarbone, for there should be three according to this form.

de la dolor dou dos	Of the great pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When great pain comes to the back, whether from striking or pressure, or from excessive evacuation, or from some similar cold, expanding substance, none of these signs warrants cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold material.

de la dolor des jointes	joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture that spreads throughout a limb, and when the pain comes in waves, they call it "gout" properly speaking, and when it is due to a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, then cautery is used as follows: make several cauterizations around the affected joint of the foot, and let the cauterization be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to prick on the face with a needle, make the cauterization all around with a claim of "no point.

And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, make cauterization on each knee with three or four cauteries from every side, all around olive-shaped; and if you need more, do so, but don't hold your hand too tightly until the heat of the heart is gone.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, apply the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
