And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the fingers with two lines; and if there is no pain at all, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give good care and purge the flu, it will be healed by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the pain
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture occurs in the intestines, and the bowels descend into the coils, it is important that when you attempt to cure it, you do not disturb them until they are healed. You should use things that leave the belly relaxed so that the intestines can descend from the belly; afterwards, make him lie on his back between your hands, and order him to keep his breath until the bowels are repaired, and arrange them in your hands, and sign with a pin the rupture on the bone of the forearm, and at any place it appears similar to half a circle above the body. Then heat the cautery as described:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and exudes scent.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their proper places; and have the attendants hold his hand so that he does not pull back; and thoroughly open the patient's thighs, and place a cushion and a support under his thighs, and another on his penis, which keeps his hands still; then apply the cautery to the sign over your entire hand, holding it straight and firm until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch the bone the first time, repeat it again until you do; be careful that the joint does not escape when you perform the cautery; do not burn him; and ensure that the patient does not die, or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cauterizer of children should be subtle according to their size, and for adults as large as them; after three days cure the wound with butter until the burning is healed; afterwards treat other wounds until they are clean, and lay the patient on his back for forty days until the wound is well sealed; and it is important that his movements be restricted for a long time so that the boils do not burst when he gets up to go to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to stand up, apply a well-made compress and repeat it for another forty days; and he should have good rest, engaging in light work and guarding against excessive drinking and eating, and also avoiding loud shouting; and following these instructions, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment for cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other abdomens and are known not to heal, you should perform cauterization with a hot iron according to its extent, either on the third day or later; then follow the treatment as we have described; and no one of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled iron in this manner.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the hernia with a sign, and make a line across the width of the rupture; then another from above, and hold your hand steady over the entire area where the hot iron will be applied.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and more manageable.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any member, whether from a fall or an injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the cure of medicine is ineffective, then it should be cauterized with the cautery known as "point," and the cautery must be applied according to the length of the member and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and its twist, and its location, and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the patient is cured by the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on the same part, for it often happens that the limb closest to it must move, so you should perform cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	It appears that the term "de meselerie" is
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	These ailments are never helped by cautery alone, especially the illness that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You can cauterize it if the illness is in its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, without delay or hesitation, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the patient, then do the following cautery: first on the head, starting from the new hair, and towards the front at the end of the beard; then on both horns, and behind on the nape; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and as far as the skin comes out, so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; cauterize it on the neck according to what is necessary.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the disease is widespread throughout, it appears clearly that you must cauterize these cauteries that we have mentioned above: first, cauterize in the armpit, then cauterize on the spine of the neck, and sixth on the spine of the back, and greatly on the cramp and another delicate one, and two on each shoulder; and two on the elbows, and two on the tender parts of the pis, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and in the pits of the hands; and beware of the nails that are on the last toe, so that you do not burn them; never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, or another on the stomach bone, or another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you perform cauterization, the greater the aid it provides and moves the patient; and know that the sick do not feel pain from cauterization as the healthy do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great or small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply flour of grains with honey and other remedies until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and bandages, but it is not completely healed, then do cautery on the member according to its size and the nature of the member; and let the cautery be slightly inside the hope of the heart; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never should cautery be done on the hand, foot, or back, at the end of the nerve that controls the member, and thus if the swelling is removed; nevertheless, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the passages of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of albaras (albaras could refer to a
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is ignited, and the medical arts are powerless against it, then cauterize with a hot iron according to the extent of the injury, until the white flesh is removed and its color changes; then apply a cure made of flour, peas, lentils, with rose oil, plantain leaves, and collic and alder sap, each in equal parts; mix them together, wrap it in a cloth, and keep it at the fire until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a ulcer (chancre) by cauterization.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a ulcer appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle around the entire edge of the ulcer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	Yet wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the ulcer; however, I do not find this good, as I fear it may become infected and corrupted, and I have never seen it work any better; and a more correct thing is to cauterize around it, with the cautery called 'circle', as we have said about many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati," and it does not kill them because of the excess it creates or due to old age, when they are debilitated (that is, too much) and have little blood, or because of time; and you see them hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; after that leave them alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	Because it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through all the cauterization, make the cautery so hot that this is its shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the midst of this ill-named 'adubelati' disease until the cauterizer has perceived the heart, and it is arranged as the cauterizer wishes, so that the patient feels freed in such a way that the course of the decay is halted.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure, until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	Heal the fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of disease is called 'corrodens', which is nothing other than a corruption of the limbs, as it attacks the members just as fire does the dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a limb that can be treated with fire cautery, then heat the cautery knives very small and large, according to what is suitable for the limb or the illness; after cauterizing from all sides until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply oil to the cauterized limb suffering from broying until all the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that cause pain.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days the wound does not heal, it is good; and if not, the cautery should be repeated on that which remains stuck in the corrupted joint.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	This mixture is sometimes cured with a sharp medicine instead of fire cautery; however, the fire cautery provides greater aid. I have already described the remedy for the sharp medicine in detail: take it as needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from the vessels that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that a piece due to deficiency develops a disease called "close" according to our intention, and it is a great fault that damages the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the treatment for this illness is according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This refers to fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	In fire cautery, you heat the cautery (a tool similar to a pen with a sharp point) over a flame until it can pierce the skin from all sides, and it has subtle edges; then apply it to the affected area, turning your hand around the entire area of the wound until it reaches the bottom of the skin. Leave it for three days so that putrefaction begins; then make a poultice with crushed mugwort and leave it on overnight. The nail will fall off and be removed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the shoulder with a healing ointment, making it clean and sound.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are turned by fire within the body, and often occur in hands and feet, it is necessary to apply hot water cautery; and this is done thus: take a rod of iron or steel, or a quill from a vulture's wing, and place the nail and the peg (that is, the splint) on it, for the treatment of warts; then place the rod over it so that it encloses everything around it, and pour some hot water upon it, holding your hand firm, and turn your hand so that the edge of the rod reaches to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep down to the root; and allow the patient to bear the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will come out with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, make one after another, until you straighten all those that are in the body, then treat the wounds that cause harm.
li cure dou trembler	It cures the shivering.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone shivers from cold or quartan fever or another illness, it is necessary that you make four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the buttocks, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; if this stops the shivering and hastens the healing from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	from the pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never is the body's health apparent through external baths or pus-filled blisters, which come from deeply corrupt materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is necessary at first to recognize when they appear that we perform cauterization on each head of the pustule: a delicate cauterization with a firestick of myrtle, from which the point is taken to the fire, or with long roots of aristologe, or with a lenticular cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should cauterization be performed at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, so that it cannot grow worse in advance, but it breaks down the excesses from which it comes, and becomes healthy; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many serious consequences arise from the blood of an artery that is cut in the wound, or in the case of a permanent opening, or incising an abscess, or cauterizing a limb, and similar things; it is a very grievous thing to become infected.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Nevertheless, if this happens to anyone, act quickly and place your index finger on the wound in the vein, and stretch it very gently until the pain subsides entirely under your touch; then take several small and large olive oil cauteries, as hot as possible, and apply them; then, according to the size of the wound and the position of the artery, place the cautery on the vein where you are holding your finger, and hold it there until the pain is completely gone.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden leap occurs while you are lying with your arm over the vein, and the cauterization is complete, then quickly take another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to apply one after the other until the wound is completely healed; be careful not to damage the nerve nearby, and ensure no further harm comes to the patient; and know that when the flow from an artery is cut off, it cannot be properly stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned: cauterization, extraction when untreated, tying it tightly with thread, or applying medications that have the power to stop blood flow; and ensure it is securely bandaged.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers relief to a tight closure with cloths or places burning objects or similar things on it, will not be successful unless he does it carefully.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he has no suitable medicine at hand, he must apply his finger directly to the wound of the vein as we have said, pressing firmly until all pain subsides from the wound and the vein; and he should not move it, but often moisten it with cold water while it remains very cold until the blood becomes congealed and thickens and stops hurting. And make inquiries about what he needs for cauterization and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every illness where it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we have explained the herbs, causes, instruments, and forms of cautery; I have placed this chapter immediately after the one on the head because it will be easier for those who wish to learn.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before we begin, it is necessary for you to know that this chapter involves greater risk and fear than the first one on cautery, and therefore requires more careful attention.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come for cure.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who have become so afflicted by their illness that they die quickly due to the severity of their condition and the magnitude of their suffering; of these one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you hope, saying, "Wait, I am whole"; but the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more great care in your honor than in your greed, and do not act rashly but wisely concerning those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can safely take and let go; and use divination and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored; and through this, you will help to gain good repute, glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most precious child, Our Lords give you good understanding and rectitude, and if you desire the holy inspiration from His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter for you, reflecting on chapters of surgery, according to the one that is before or at the end of the chapter on cautery, which I have devised from head to foot, so that you may find it easier to understand what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Dou chief plein d'aigue" translates to "a head full of blood
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the head of the child is too tightly compressed, it never happens for a reason that one can discern.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease but in children, and to all those that I have seen, death comes quickly; and for this reason, I think it is best to leave the work in parts for treatment.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw children whose joints were filled with water, and the head became swollen each day until it could not be supported; the moisture was so great that it caused death, and this moisture is collected under the bone next to the sinew, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, so you must make a wide cut in the head until the moisture flows out; and it should be as long as necessary, until the moisture has drained; and see the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more severe, and the abscess larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is between the bones, and you see the openings of the sinuses on each side of the head wide open, and there is a sharp, strong flow when you press with your hand inside, and it does not return to its place, then you must make three cuts in the middle of the head in this way:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the cracks of drapes and powders, and applying wine and oil, leave it thus for up to five days; then loosen it, and dress the wound with bandages and plasters, and stretch the head equally, and give the patient dry meat from a bag of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe or measure the size of the abscess and the arrangement of the fluid; for it never appears in front, nor behind, nor on the right, nor on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So measure the abscess and the amount of fluid, and cut according to your ability; be careful not to block the artery; then comes flux of blood, so that the patient dies slowly from the flow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of the root
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a condition called "cataract" in one or both eyes, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the final remedy is cauterization by sealing the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you have sealed their eyes, the patient should turn their head away; then rub the affected area with a rough cloth until the arteries open, and gently pull the skin away from the eye with all your cloth; then observe where the vein is located, and mark the positions of the limbs behind the ears, and make sure they are relaxed; then sign the areas to be cauterized, and use a sharp instrument to cut both arteries, reaching as deep as the bone, making incisions across the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, remove the spatule beneath the artery and cut through the covering above, cutting as it should go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when pressed, it is necessary to measure the space with three fingers, then seal it with a string and make it extend to the bone; and this amount of blood, it is six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear and the filling of the artery. Then attend to the wound: if there is no discharge from pus on the bone, cut open the wound and bind it, and treat with medication until it heals.
de emigrainne	from migraine headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine headache occurs, accompanied by catarrh, due to moisture in the eyes and sockets, and ancient fatigue and similar symptoms, it is treated with various medical cures, but often without success. Therefore, we drain the arteries of the eyes and apply cautery, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from his temples and locates the artery that opens in the temple, as it opens clearly due to its pulsation, and is protected from being seen by anyone who is not an expert. If it is exposed, the patient gently squeezes some cloth around it, then rubs the area with a rough cloth, and soaks it in hot water until the artery becomes visible; then take the spatula with this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scrape the skin gently until you reach the artery, then treat it with pincers, and carefully separate the threads that hold it in each part; and if the artery is thin, twist it to the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not heal at all without pain.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the blood from the sixth to the third; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you bind it with two strong silk threads so that no pus comes before the wound heals, and no further bleeding occurs; then cut off the excess between the two threads at the same time, and if you see fit, cauterize the wound with a hot iron until the bones are cut through; this is the moving part, if the patient does not have fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery is aid to finish off moisture: for this reason it is of greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract arteries, one should fill the space with thick cotton and place several well-made bandages; and when they are loosened, take care to apply dry medicines that produce heat, and bandage again until healed; and if there is no delay in treating the artery, hasten to cover it with cautery, or use vitriole (a caustic substance) and press with your hand so that the wound is cleansed; and if you do not have this at hand, put snow on the wound until the bleeding stops, and gently press as needed; and in the extraction of arteries, it is better to cauterize the vein from both sides, but the cuts should be well-spaced to preserve their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they do not hold their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have a sufficient space between the two blades, and then, when you have sealed the two joints, place the hot iron over until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be far apart between the two joints, because this cautery is not properly joined in every way; and this is the shape of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are on the top of the head, and no medicine helps, you see the face of the patient contort, feeling as if from a cold, and the skin is tense and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called this the ancient "scab cure," and what you do for the patient suffering from this disease is to shave the hair on their forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead evenly according to its length; one of the cuts goes all the way across the front, down to the nose, and the other two cuts are made along the sides, above the eyelids, but beware of incising the arteries that are by the side. Keep your hand away from the continuity of the jawbones, and let each wound be as deep as three fingers across; then take a piece of sponge and cloth to wipe away the blood, and use the spatula (in the shape shown) for this purpose.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple up to the second incision; then scrape all the flesh that is between the two cuts to the full satisfaction that is on the bone, then make another from the middle incision up to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called "cultellaire" (a type of scalpel) into the first cut, it should be very sharp on one side and soft on the other; this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the sharp side of the instrument towards the opposite edge (of the bone) and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the joints, so that the incision is continuous until it opens towards the heart, and then make another narrow slit until it reaches the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and press out the blood through a cloth; then place a piece of old cotton in each slit, and cover them with damp cloths dipped in wine, oil, and ash, and ensure that no abscesses form; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer a strong infusion of water, then apply basilicon treatment with rose oil, and other remedies to heal wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	dou reume des eulz (in this context) translates to "until the
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	As for any sudden catarrh that is accustomed to coming, and you see the thick and small ones, weakening the sight, and burning the papers; and the hair falls out, and it feels as if a sharp pain is piercing in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that this matter and this catarrh do not come from one but many veins, and the moving cure that is there, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to bend his forehead backward, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another one quite wide.

And begin from the cut in the left temple to the right temple, making the incision down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerve of the temples that move when you blink. de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear inflammation
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes pain in the ears is one of four things: grains, animals, minerals or similar objects; seeds such as beans, peas; or fluid-like substances such as water and ice, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	If anything, such as a stone or any other object that does not adjust to the ear or grow in the ear, is inserted into the ear, it should be removed and the ear exposed to sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, and it distills any little drop of purple oil or frankincense oil, then it is ready for extraction; and the act causes a sneeze from the condition, and it stops the nostrils when sneezing occurs, and places pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear, and stretches the ear towards the top.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times this treatment brings fever; and if it does not bring fever, then extraction is performed with delicate pincers, like this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If the extraction with pincers brings fever, that is good; if not, perform extraction with an intricate, small instrument with a double edge; and if it still does not bring fever, make a chain of aram and close the top of the chain around the ear hole tightly, and stuff what's around the chain with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the chain; then treat it thoroughly, because fever often follows in this manner; and if it does not come about in this way, take great care to remove all debris, and insert a pointed instrument where necessary, and place a little cotton inside; then press the clot onto the stone or something similar, and treat it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not follow all these things that we have said, then hasten to pierce the ear so that the abscess hardens and calms; and the manner of piercing is as follows: you must first cleanse the patient with the headache, extract the blood according to its strength, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, making a small cut at the base of the ear where the fat or tissue is attached; let the cut be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck on it with your mouth; and the cure as long as it remains healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains present and they swell, then perform extraction; and if they cannot be extracted, then use a delicate knife according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not attempt this if you think the grain is moist from earwax, having made many attempts; then extract it with subtle tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case that something has entered the ear, have the patient use a gentle sneeze, and open the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear, or the water is inside.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps through the fire, it is good.

de la char des papieres	concerning the use of papers

de la gresle	(without context it's difficult to provide an accurate translation, but based
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to paper certain things that seem grim in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "frost," and it is a gathering of great moisture on the paper above and below; the work is as follows: be vigilant if the frost becomes silent from one side to the other, and this is a slight thing to know; then make them wide, and scrape each part lightly, and take them with pincers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover them without piercing the paper slightly, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the split is great, and the gathering has a stitch, treat it as long as it remains healthy; but if it is small, make no strong effort, for the adhesions will restore it soon enough and cause trouble.

And if the pain is descending inside the ear towards the top part, turn the paper against it, and the pain will grip with pinches, and the heat and pressure from both sides; and when the paper is removed by incision, it causes no harm; and once the pain is cut away, lift the salt water to wash out the wound until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes

The condition is a fat that is embedded in the skin beneath the paper, and it occurs more often in children than adults, causing great pain to their eyes, and leading to cataracts in the mornings, preventing them from gazing the light of the sun because tears constantly flow from their eyes; and due to this, they rest their faces on their hands, sleeping on them, and the fat beneath their eyebrows becomes swollen and appears as if it has been opened by the exinac (presumably referring to a type of eye condition or inflammation).

des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hair grows abnormally in papers (scalp) other than its natural state, it becomes irritated, causing harm and leading to conditions similar to scabs and mollifications of the papers (skin), and albugine (a type of skin condition), as long as it is caused by the destruction of the hairs; and the cure is according to four methods: either with fire cautery altogether, or with acute medicine according to what is mentioned in the preceding chapter on cautery, or through incision and stitching, or with bands, as I will explain.

puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take those who are weak and equalize their small forces according to this form:

de la porriture de l’oil	regarding the impurity of oil

And the secret of your cure lies in ensuring it does not harden according to its former shape; and these remedies that we have mentioned are only proper measures for this illness, so that it does not return in the same way as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the grease that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocation, truly called "axacrati," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidental dislocation arises from wounds, incisions, cauterization, and similar events; and the method of treatment in such cases is that if you insert an needle, it should have a double thread, and be driven into the flesh on the left side as if it were to the right, so that the thread passes through both sides of the skin; then the skin is pulled taut over the entire needle, and the wound covered with a large bandage.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the shape of the skin returns to its proper place, that is good; if not, take a razor and insert it into the gap, turn the skin, and make two cuts on either side of the incision you made, so that the edges of these cuts form two angles with the incision, creating a shape similar to the letter 'g' in Greek. Then remove the bandage, according to the extent of the displacement on both sides of the skin, from where we previously attached the paper, then adjust the two parts back into their proper positions and sew them together with a thread of wool. Finally, apply the treatments we have mentioned regarding mollifying medicines and poultices until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness arises from cutting, stitching, or cauterization, it is necessary to make a clean cut beneath the skin among the hairs, and according to what has been said before; then separate the two leaves of a blade, as I have explained; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it varies greatly in form, and skilled physicians devise various instruments to restore the natural shape, and the patients themselves, according to what is appropriate for the operation and the tools available.
dou soudement de la papiere	The phrase "dou soudement de la papiere" does not have a clear or straightforward
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this cauterization takes place in a familiar way that the paper on top is smooth with white oil, and it cannot move nor perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it up; extend it as pincers, until you remove what is hard in the delicate spatula, neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient does not suffer from a spatula that is too sharp or bleeds oil; make your incision gently, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and all of the attached paper heals, without ever leaving saltiness in the oil, or bringing up water from fresh wounds, and then place between the paper and the oil a thin cloth of linen, and on top of the oil lay moist wool in abundance; after the third day, use cologne and things that promote healing until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You know that the nail has two manners: one is nervous and resembles a hard and smooth surface, and another which is not nervous but appears as white, frozen moisture, which, when touched with iron and treated with pliers, no one can do; and both of them begin towards the great tear, growing little by little until they cover the whole sight, light, and movement of the finger.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The method of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in a healthy position, then opens the joint; takes a piece of paper in their hand, then coils the nail with pliers, extending it upwards; takes an needle, threads a horsehair, or a sinew from a cow or bull onto it, and doubles the tip of the needle, piercing it through the nail entirely, and securing it with thread, stretching it upwards, and scraping all the hair alongside the nail root with a sharp blade, down to the tear duct, leaving the natural shape of the tear duct intact so that the incision does not cause tears; never stretch the nail directly against the clock, only using thread as we have said; then scrape off all the soft tissue around it, giving it this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be sure that the scalpel does not touch and tear the soft flesh, and that the wound is not pierced; afterwards, after incising, pour a little of the ground silk into the oil, and make a bandage from it with lithargyrum, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot push the needle, and the hooks cannot enter, often this appearance of a nail requires treatment with medicines; as I have described in the previous section, if you see it covered, open the wound gently for the patient, and take the scalpel lightly according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And cut the nail from above gently, and if you see that it becomes weak and the reason is pressed, it distills from your mouth into a collar made of collyrium (eye drops) of litargire and with a red collar, and stop the oil until the next day; then repeat the other work according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing contradicts you about the oil, such as a hot abscess, then apply it, and treat first the hot abscess until it is healed, and then continue the work as before, until it is completely cured.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh causes pain in the eye by great damage, suspending it at the corner and cutting off a part but not all of it, so that tears do not come; then distill into the eye a red collyre made of lithargy.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	on the flesh that is born on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some people are born without any red flesh on their eyelids, covering and restraining the pupil within the papilles, resembling a rosebud; and this is so effective that the patient can place his head in a healthy position. Then open the eyes and gently pull all the flesh as suitable with the proper force, and cut off the first piece, shaving it down to the bare surface until the end of the process, taking care not to hurt the eye during the procedure. After the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, apply oil of seal or any other medicine that we have mentioned for cutting a nail and similar small forces, shaping the area as demonstrated in this chapter; then soak a piece of cotton in hot oil and place it over the affected area to ensure warmth. If there is no improvement or if the condition worsens, leave the oil and treat the warm aposteme with soothing remedies. Then return to your work until it is healed. This is how all such cuts should be made on the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, you must pay attention to the treatment of each weak oil in the natural path; and in the accidental path, in the work of iron; and do not push your hand into any of these works as long as you see that this member suffers from this work.
des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are the red veins that are covered over the eye, and they steal from the sight their work and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Skillful is the first that you observe this eye, as it is red, swollen, and there is no other disease outside of the redness; then take these steps: instruct the patient to place their head on your healthy side, then suspend those veins throughout the entire circumference according to your wisdom, and make the incisions delicate in double layers following this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And there should be two incisions according to degrees in the body following this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, gently coil the veins and wipe off the blood hour after hour until you remove the veins from the flesh; be careful not to damage the oil with the edges of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your task so that you do not stop until the veins are removed; and when you have done this, distil green and red collyre into the oil to corrupt what remains from the sebum.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all of them in that hour, make a poultice over the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for no more than a day until the pain is eased and the hot abscess is assured, then continue according to this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of the veins:
de la fistule de l’oil	from the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	He observes if they call it "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and acute medicine as I have previously mentioned, and it does not heal, there is a force within it that you must cut into the abscess, where it is destined to die, and remove all the moisture until the bone becomes exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone becomes exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the instruments mentioned here and shape them; it is called "sharp point", and it should be made from iron from head to tip, and pointed like a file as shown in the current form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the corrupt bone back in its position, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you know that corruption is gone; do this several times, then return the joint to its medicinal state.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joints are fused and it appears that the bowel is also fused, leave it in that state for 40 days, and it will heal and there will be no abscess; be aware that no bad accidents will occur, knowing that it is healthy. If not, there is another way to bring the fistula back to the opening with a knife according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron or medicine, and when it is uncovered, take a forge as shown here, and make three angles in the iron, and narrow it from the top as you can see.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the delicate bone of the arm, and move your hand away from the wound, then continue all the way around until it pierces the bone and causes the patient pain because they hold their hand close to their body; and then return to using dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the charring and hardening of the bones has occurred, then examine the matter at the joint; if it is a lighter task for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the wound
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.
