When the wound is completely open and does not disturb or narrow the passageway, it is necessary to keep the patient still; then apply a healthy dressing, followed by leeching cups or a plaster without causing injury, then cover it with oil made from aloe, myrrh, and incense, and bind it tightly. After allowing the oil to draw out for some time, wrap bandages and cloth around it; and make sure these are soft enough, doubled up in layers of four, and arranged one on top of the other according to the needs of the wound. Then reapply the leeching cups without causing injury, and continue with the poultices, bandages, and bindings tightly for a whole day and night, and check if it becomes easier; if so, remove the bindings during the day and night, and if you see the oil being absorbed, that is good. If not, repeat the poultices, bandages, and bindings until the wound heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	loss of fabric integrity
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When there is a tear in the fabric, it opens and allows threads to protrude like resin grains, which is encouraging to observe. If you see this, take a needle and pierce it through the root of the affected part down to the layer above, then insert another needle where the thread forms a double loop, and pierce it. Leave the first needle in place, cut off the thread with the double loop, and tie a piece of the fabric around it, pulling it tightly, then remove the needle and apply fresh, moist lint to the wound until the thread is fully absorbed, and treat the wound with soothing remedies until the injury heals; at no time should the wound be restricted by the fabric in any circular pattern until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the joint appears well-formed, use a fine spatula to pierce it, and drain the white, cloudy moisture, and then reduce it, and extract it as soon as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the fat of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not caused by any fluid gathered in the oil, resembling clear water, but it is not clear; and the manner of its appearance in the work is that you place the patient in a sitting position with their back straight, then take the head between your hands from two sides, and move it until you see the fat rise up to their joints; then insert a needle, and do not let any light escape, and have the patient look at things as they normally would; if the fluid does not drain out, know that it is acute, and the movement of the fat downward is not arranged as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient rest between your hands, then take the delicate instrument and make incisions on the corneal membrane along the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal membrane and cornea, until the bowel is released; and when it has been discharged, it distills into clear hot oil mixed with honey, or boiling fennel seed and honey, then apply another remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	The phrase "des aigues de l’oil" translates directly to "of the waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have similar waters in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; doing so according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should let the patient rest with their sore hand between your crossed hands, away from direct sunlight, and apply pure oil and hold it tightly; then place the paper of the oil in your left hand if the joints are on the left side, or in your right hand if they're on the right; then take the instrument called 'almagda' in your right hand if the joints are on the left, or your left hand if they're on the right; then insert the tip of the instrument into the thickest part of the blenchor (skin) of the oil, at the outer corner of the eye, and press it firmly until you feel the almagda reach the empty space; and the length of the almagda should be equal to the measurement of the distance from the prunelet (small fruit) to the end of the night (blackness); that is the blenchor of the oil. You will see the bone on the paper due to the clarity of the corneal skin, then place the instrument up to its base or where the water is, and express it through one channel after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he lowers himself now, let him see the patient before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, lower yourself again along the second path, insert the instrument, and when it is firmly wedged and does not move upwards, slowly extract it by turning your hand back and forth; then lift it up again with a little force, removing the oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply hot oil or any other moist oil (roses) and an abundance of heat, and wrap it with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place a fine, new bandage with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the foreign body cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are many people with very hard eyelids, it is necessary that you press the instrument called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva gently, and do not cut too deeply, but make a slight opening, then insert the foreign body as we have said; and after the work is complete, prepare the patient for sleep with a comfortable position on his back in a dark place; and be careful of all movements, press lightly on soft flesh, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition for three days. Then release him in the same dark room, test his vision, and make him see no objects, and then re-bind him for seven days; and it is not appropriate that you perform this at the time of treatment or after incision now, but it is appropriate to ease him, because the sharp pain rises suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess forms, you should loosen the skin in front of the seventh day and apply the remedies that soothe the abscess; and once it is soothed, unfasten the view and place a corner of cloth on its face to cover for some time, and then return it to that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he should leave the house little by little and recover from his illness; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And then one came to us from Iraq, who told us that in his land they use a certain tool to suck out water, but I have never seen anyone use it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that he who does not know them will see them as different; and they must be of gold precisely.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the front of this same subtlety be sharp, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the charm on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No charm should be born or made with diverse arrangements, for there is none that seems like a scorpion in its movement; and if there are such where a charm is adorned with bright colors, or one that has a smooth charm of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the wound is fresh and not yet healed, you must place the patient between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and apply the ointment to those parts, and treat them fiercely; but hold what you can sustain with a delicate knife on one side, until you know that part is entirely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, open it with all delicate and light instruments until nothing is left; and without delay, perform the operation as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood is drained and all parts are healed, then apply heat or cold and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you open it and moisture appears in the wound, knowing that it is clean; and if the moisture does not drain as it should, knowing there is something stuck in the bone above, preventing the tools from cutting: then you must insert a piece of linen thread, thick enough, and tie it with our hands, leaving some space between each knot, and put the patient's foot in the thread to their ability, drawing it out while smelling until it comes out through the wound inside the mouth; and often children are so taught, and it is an easy task for whoever wishes to do it. Then hold the part that comes through the wound with one hand, and the other part coming from the mouth with the other hand, feeling them alternately as we who are in thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as you know, purify the affected area, then treat the wound, dry it with an Egyptian ointment, and put the bandage back in place; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded all that remains of the impurities. Then, for a few days, keep the wound covered with a clean poultice, and if any dried medicine needs to be applied, do so; this is the form of the instrument used to purge the head, through which oils and medicines are distilled into the wound.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and use it thus; if you see, make a closed cane, and let the instruments be full for purging the head; have many around the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there appears near the nose a disease called "telul," which swells and becomes very large, so much so that it is a sight to behold; and for this reason, it is necessary that you remove it at the beginning, clean it thoroughly, then apply hot cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay removing it until it becomes large, be wary if it has a hard, dark color, poor sensation: do not touch it with iron, because it is an abscessed joint, for whenever you remove it, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is sensitive, not dark colored, and you are able to completely remove it without pain, then empty the patient and remove it carefully, using dry things and restraining movements.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the continuation of one of these powerful cartilages is broken, it benefits no one.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this happens to no one, then consider that if the wound is fresh, you should stitch both lips together, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips have already separated on both sides, it is necessary to scrape all parts of their heart while they are healing, then stitch them together again, and tighten them, and apply dragon's blood powder and incense powder; and place a piece of strong or other adhesive plaster over the powders, and leave it until it sticks by itself, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is such that you bring the wound together: either with needles, as we have said in sewing the stomach; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, the abscesses on the lips become hard, resembling small grains of various sizes, then you must turn the lips and make incisions in each one, taking them as pincers and pressing each part; then apply the medicine afterward with a piece of glass ground into powder, until the wound is stained; then use a dry leaf, and treat the wound with things to remove dryness until it heals.
de la char des gencives	from the work of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a growth appears on the gums, which the old call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with pliers and cut it at its root, allowing the bowel or the blood to flow; then apply powder of vitriol or other astringent and desiccating powders; if the growth returns after the incision, this happens often, especially if the piece is cut again, and cauterize it: if it does not return after cauterization; these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	from disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth are ever aligned at the root within the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and no teeth are black and yellow and rotten, as long as the corruption reaches the gums, and they stink; it is necessary that you hold the patient's teeth in your hands, and their roots in a clean place, and pull out the teeth or gums that appear, until nothing remains; and do this with the black ones and green ones, and jaundice and others until they are completely extracted; and if something is left at the first attempt, it is good; if not, continue to try again on the second day and third, until everything is pulled out; and know that teeth require various tools to pull them out, according to what the work shows, because the cutter used to remove them from between the teeth has different shapes than that used to pull them out. These shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should take care when treating a toothache and do not delay in drawing it out as much as you can, for no one should excuse themselves from doing so; for it is a very precious substance indeed.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is constrained from drawing out the tooth, it is necessary that you be certain about which tooth is painful.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient complains of pain, believing it to be from a tooth that is healthy, and has the good tooth drawn out; however, the pain does not cease because of this, as we have seen with these saints; and when you are certain about which tooth is painful, it is necessary to scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gums on all sides; then move the pliers to the first slight movement, as much as possible, until they are well positioned, and then tighten the pliers; place the patient's head between your knees, holding the tooth firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take none of these instruments and press it gently from every side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is broken and scattered, it is necessary that you fill the space between or around the missing tooth with cloth; if you pull it out gently with tweezers, so as not to break it while pulling; and it must be done very carefully around the gums to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take good care so as not to break it, and if a piece remains, return it to the patient; by the evil of its root, he will suffer greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be sure you do not act like the ignorant healers who, in their haste and arrogance, break the patient's body, and do not take heed of what we have said, but bring about the death of a great sickness through their carelessness, or by breaking the bones they should leave whole; when the bone is dislocated, wash it with wine or aloe and silk. And the flow of blood often comes, which frequently happens if you apply vitriol; if not, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shape of the instruments used to extract teeth should be long and sharply pointed, with thick handles that do not bend when pulling a tooth; these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large members so that they do not bend when pulled, and made of iron well-forged, and toothed for proper movement.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck when pulled, it is necessary to place cotton moistened with butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the eyes are moistened, then apply pliers called 'algefri', which make the joint look like it is being cared for; they should be made inside like a file and this is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of these grips, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called "altali," that is, a plier, which has this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is strong and thick so that it does not break, and the root jumps out through this, that is good. If not, use all the instruments, whose forms are as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two prongs, its form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are used in the treatment of teeth, and this tool that resembles large pincers, whose form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	This tool should be of such sturdy construction that it cannot break, and you must know that many tools for teeth exist; likewise, there are other tools, not mentioned here. The most skilled surgeons invent their own instruments, according to what their work and the patient's condition show them, because there are certain diseases for which no instrument was taught by the ancients due to the diversity of symptoms. If a fragment breaks off or becomes stuck in another bone, or if it splinters, and the patient seeks the appropriate tools I have described, using gestures, then this is their form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return the limb to suitable medicine for this, and if there is decay in the bone, even small, use all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth does not appear according to the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the normal teeth and is not in the right place, and it cannot be cut or filed. Then extract it; and if it grows with another tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and made of sharp steel.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the dentist should work slowly and carefully with his hands for the pain of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as the shape allows.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like filing the metal from which they make needles; file the tooth slowly and carefully with your hands until it does not move any more, then plane it at the end with no rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp, it cuts the tongue, it is necessary to file its roughness so that it is even, so as not to cut or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth aches intensely, either by impact or pulling, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it, they suffer greatly, and medications do not help. They should be restrained with an oro-dental device; gold wire is better than silver as it does not tarnish or rot. The wire should neither be too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth. If you align the teeth, take a length of wire longer than the distance between two healthy teeth, then place the roots of the painful teeth into the wire gap, one by one, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side. Continue covering in this manner, gently and carefully applying pressure until the tooth stops moving. Ensure your pliers are at the root of the tooth to prevent it from escaping.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the tendons with pliers, assemble them, and reconnect them between the healthy tooth and place it so that the tongue does not bleed; and then leave it as tight as possible for as long as it can stay, and if it becomes loose, the threads will unravel, if it is held by another thread; it should hold firm and serve for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the correct arrangement of the two healthy molars, and the two incisors, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is dislodged, put it back in its place, freshly broken, as we have said; and let no one intervene unless they are wise and patient, and never make a shape of an ossified tooth from veal bone, and place it where there is a defect, and hold it as we have said, keeping it firm and serving for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	from cutting the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never does this ligament come from below the tongue, naturally, but it is cut either by a deep wound or accidentally; and the work consists of opening the mouth of the patient with great care, and holding his head so that it remains in your hands, then lifting the tongue and cutting the nervous ligament with a large knife, as far as the tongue is detached from its place, and if there is any hardness or resistance, and this is due to a sudden wound, then use the hook and cut through the ligament; be careful that the incision does not go too deep, for the artery below. And once you have done this, raise the affected area with rosewater or icy water, and place a linen bandage under the tongue; apply this bandage to the patient each night so that the ligaments do not adhere.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood flow occurs, place a hot, crushed glass over it; and if the wound bleeds profusely, apply a slow-burning cauterizing tool, which is good for this; then treat with another remedy until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it is red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, as it is a cancer; and if it turns pale and there is moisture, drain it with a fine needle, and make an incision with a small spatula, and deliver it from both sides; and if the wound bleeds profusely during your work, apply hot, crushed glass until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you have treated everything thoroughly. Then lift the limb gently and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No sign of abscesses should appear inside the throat, which are called "godath," and we properly call them "II amandres." When treating them, as we have discussed in the previous section, be careful: if they are small and of a deep red color, do not touch them with metal.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with metal, also to prevent the spread of infection; but leave it until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it may break on its own. If they are white in color and the root is thin, prepare an instrument to extract it, but first ensure that the abscess is calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and keep his feet in a healthy position, and open the mouth, and press the tongue down with the instrument between his hands, pressing it from side to side, so that this is the shape; and use silver or fine gold as if it were a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You cannot press the tongue with all of this instrument and observe the abscess, so take the chisel and drill into it, pulling it upward as much as you can; do not touch any parts of the threads with it, then cut it off with the instrument, forming a shape that resembles teeth; however, the head is bent in one place and another, very sharp, and made of hard iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pincers, thus is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	It should be cut on one side and named; and when you have extracted one of the mandibles, extract the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's mouth with hot water and water mixed with salt and some herbs, such as pomegranate peels, myrrh, or similar substances, until the blood is stopped. Then apply the cure while it is still fresh; and no other abscesses will form in the throat except for these two mandibles, if they are extracted in this way as with the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was located inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and the whole throat was tightly closed so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained that way for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed two ribs through the two openings in the throat where it entered.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a knife into one of the openings, and pulled it through, taking out a large portion of the abscess; I then did the same in the other opening, opening the mouth and pressing the tongue; after inserting the knife into the abscesses and removing some of the pus, only a little blood came out, and thus the passageway in the throat was cleared for her to begin drinking water and then wine. I continued cutting into the abscess for a long time, and the abscess refilled again, filling up the space that I had emptied out, becoming quite large; then I cauterized it inside the throat, and it stopped growing. Thus, she recovered; and I parted from these tasks, and only God knows what came afterward.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eye swells and turns red, and it is distant from its socket, it is called "perpendicular"; but if it is thin and round, it is called "eye.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have stated in the previous section, but the cure does not help, and you see that the abscess is calm, and it is subtle, then you should drain it; the round one that is not distant. It is bloody or of a deep red or black color, so be careful with incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the sick person.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So it is necessary, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, to lay the sick person before the sun and press the tongue with the instrument of which we spoke earlier; then insert the pin in the wound, pull it out from the inside, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for incising the mandrils.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut off more than the surplus beyond the natural limit; for if you cut too much, it grieves the voice and speech. After the incision, use what we said regarding incising the mandrils, and treat it as long as it remains healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient suffers from great pain, it is necessary that you use an instrument for cauterization to alleviate the sensitive pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization must be sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place his head in a healthy position and then press his tongue against the instrument mentioned in this chapter (cauterization), using it with sharp, hot iron, so that it is not too thick or too thin; and by using this instrument, as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the chief physician have a cheveure (a kind of instrument), as if holding the handle of a spoon, and place the tool over all the medicine on the eye; and have the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus from their mouth flow down into the medicine without reaching the throat or causing harm; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it stop bubbling and the stings of the medicine are soothed; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around a tool, soak it in the medicine, and press the tool into the cotton against the eye socket until the cotton sticks to the eye; repeat this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and after three or four days, or five, if you need to reapply the cautery, do so, and afterwards wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in burped butter, and clean what's around the medicine; rise with cold water, and make gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than cautery or incision; if it is performed through fumigation in this manner, take calamint, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, and similar herbs, and combine them all or any of them in a pot, and place it there, and make it boil; the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and have a cheveit (a type of instrument) placed inside it according to this manner.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be either of silver or gold, and one of the joints should be squeezed in the mouth of the patient as the vapor rises to the eye through the nostril, until the eye becomes numb; afterward, it often recurs as long as the eye is dry. Be careful not to perform this at the onset of a hot abscess, as many complications can arise; only do this when the hot abscess declines.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and insert within the mouth a piece of cold iron, so that it does not burn too hot for the patient; for the piece of cold iron does not allow the steam to weigh down the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether beneficial.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a sore throat is caused by bone or a splinter of fish, or some other object. Therefore, you should treat what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument so that you may observe the thing; and if it does not open and is withdrawn from the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patients might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread, and then suck on it; and when it comes to the throat, it will become sore, and then you can extract it forcefully. And if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of plunk according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And take the sharp instrument to the throat so that it can enter more easily, and lift the head high; be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that all of it does not come down, and do not push the bone inside; let the patient push the instrument, for then it will move where the thing is stuck; if it goes down, pull it out evenly throughout the instrument until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the throat treated with medicine, as I said in the previous section, except through medicinal treatment; and if that does not help, then look at the throat of the sick person against the light, press the tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, draw it out with all its tiny hooks, or subtle pincers that are fit for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a horsehair rope and tie it around the throat of the patient, then slowly tighten or loosen the rope until the vein heats up and this is done often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is filled with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in until they swallow it, moving their hand often; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will close.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, and infuses the patient with bad smell from the instrument used in the fumigation of the eye, do this many times, for it will eventually fall without resistance.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: you light a pot with hot coals, place a perforated cover over it, and put the instrument for fumigation in the hole. Then pour your fumigant, and make the patient put the cane in his mouth and close his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but goes directly to his lungs; and the coughing will now begin, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times. Let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not let him drink water; then it will be necessary for him to cough up phlegm through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it is visible, resembles a curved pliers designed to enter the throat; and it looks like a bird's beak, and has the hardness of lime, so that whatever it catches, it cannot let go; and see this shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Various forms of abscesses are, as memory recalls from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two manners, one being in its own likeness, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the upper part is different from that of the lower, and the abscess of the fleshy part of the shoulder is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if, for an abscess, one should not pierce the skin until the bowel is completely healed, according to its completion; but for such as require piercing when they are hardened, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are in the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from damaged joints, and they are left as they are until the pus is drained, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, leading to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is in the main member and you delay draining it while it is still fresh, it will harm the principal member; or if it is from the foundation, you must pierce it in such a way that it does not spread further, so as not to cause fistulas and prevent healing completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of perforating an abscess that is killed according to completion, and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the pain and redness diminish, and the swelling and sharpening of the abscess's head, and other signs; and you must make the perforation depend more on the abscess, and where it opens moves; and the perforation should be long in the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and muscles, and arteries, and everywhere equally without any swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When these swellings occur, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when there are abscesses in soft flesh, it is better to let the incision heal completely before moving it, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before the wound has healed, the body will fill with harmful pus, and the lips may harden and become attached to it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced according to the thickness of the flesh and the part that the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary to treat small abscesses with small incisions; and for large abscesses, large incisions, and many slits according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that require a heart-shaped incision, do so; and when they have become as wide as the cloth and are softened, proceed as with boils: and if there are such that are split into three angles, or such that are treated like the fleece of myrtle, like the abscesses of enemies; and if there are such where a round cut is made, other cuts, and similar shapes.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no head, if the abscess is painful on the surface, it is necessary that you pierce it deeply; and when the abscess is large and has a great curvature, and you pierce it, do not extract all the pus at once in that moment, but only part of it; then bandage the abscess until the next day, and afterward take nothing from above; repeat this many times little by little until all the pus comes out; especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old, decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For often the patient will jump with the release of the pus, and by chance might die, and you will not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if the wound has drained, and observe whether the abscess is small; and if it is a deep wound, apply linement or old cotton thread; but if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should put a tent in each so that they come together. And if you have reached into the abscess a piece of hard skin, and sealed it around, you should fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then open it, and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the progression of blood occurs in your work, apply cold water and ice, wet the cloth, and repeatedly place it on the affected area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, provide proper management and treatment, and use the powders I mentioned in this book, and apply them to the wound or abscess, especially when they are very sensitive; then place moist cloths of wine and hot oil on top. And if it is in a state where the flesh is still fresh, lay moist cloths of cold water and oil, or fresh wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; then remove the abscess and clean and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have already told you how you should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and now here is this chapter.
des soros	From the sources
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or consider how small boils come, which are like our skin's threads, just as the joiner of a woman's garment, and there are many of these appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are large and such, containing moisture as well as pulsation; and if it is of the kind that is hard and resistant to cutting, then there is no doubt that the arteries do not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of size is such that you must try all instruments called "entromissory", from which the form comes as follows, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, and they open it from above down, it causes pain.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, if scraping leaves no trace on the skin containing the moisture, it will repeatedly return unless something is left there; then apply cotton with Egyptian ointment if it is available; if not, use water and silk, and dress the wound, leaving it until the next day; and this corrects what has been delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then recommence the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, as long as you are certain it does not remain during the night; then dress the wound with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is firm and holds tightly, following this form, then press it longwise; pour on the ointments, scrape from all sides, and do your best to draw out the pus from the wound where it lies; and if the artery reacts against you, then do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same for an abscess that is deep, and cut and cure it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the deep and moist abscess, which is lighter because they have less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if none of these abscesses or sores has any moisture, and it was one of these future abscesses that I treated on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard, sharp, and white as a stone, and unbreakable; and if anyone had tried to break it, they would have caused just as much harm as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other cases of abscesses on the head, those that appear at the top of the head and at the roots of the ears, they should be left open for as long as possible near their base to allow the pus to drain; and the cure should be performed as necessary.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and dissolves the adhesions, and engenders anger, and never comes elsewhere in the body, and is painful, and severely entangled with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its bone, as we have said, both the new and the abscess from the head, and there are many appearances of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some of these contain moisture, and some are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that which you see of good disposition for the touch, resembling the color of healthy flesh, and silent from every side, not open as a wound in the collar or artery or vessel, and not too deep; it is necessary that you cover it from above, and peel from each part, and the two lips of the heart are thus, if it is needed, as we have said in the chapters on the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, nor let your tools slip, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cover something that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cover the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, apply vitriole (a corrosive substance) ground into powder, or any powders that stop blood flow, and tighten the wound; leave it until the inflammation is calmed and the wound softened, and then begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, it returns to your work until you complete it; then pay close attention to your signs if there are no small scabs, clean and dry them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the abscess, it is not enough that you clean this abscess at its root, but tie it with a double thread strong and leave it hanging without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you clean the entire abscess, it is necessary that you close the two edges of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no unnecessary delay due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary for you to understand how to treat the root of the dislocation, pull it firmly, and dress it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scrofulas that have an excess, drain it where it appears to be closing in; and drain it thus as mentioned before, depending on the condition, then apply these treatments with dressings and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what is left from the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, continue the healing treatment with care, until it is healed.
de squinance	squinance (Old French) translates to "dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They old ones spoke and discussed about the surgery of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and it is their scriptures that record their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary to avoid the fold in the throat called "epiglote"; and one should not attempt to help them, because all the veins and the pores of the sick person are close to each other in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the tongue, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to prevent the damage that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.
