It is necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it in three circles or four small incisions across, between the two circles or according to the depth of the incision, not into the cartilage; and these cuts are very suitable for cutting through the epiglottis as there is no fat, and the vessel is long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to the whole circle, then cuts through the heart as it reaches the chain, and avoids the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cuts through the fat, as we have said; and it is proven by cutting the flow of the chain that comes out from the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leaves the wound open in a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound together where the heart is, and cut through until you reach the cartilage; then administer medications that promote healing, as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasim (a surgical tool) should not be used unless the throat is completely sealed, and the patient is judged to be near death, as it lacks the necessary strength.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then they should cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, so that death is averted; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to keep the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, either in three days or four. And then they ordered the wound to be sutured and treated, as long as it was healing; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took a knife and stabbed it into her throat, cutting through part of the glands in the neck; and I was called to cure her, but I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and realized that it had no power to reach the veins or flow into the throat; the only outlet was through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I acted quickly and sewed up the wound, treating it until it was healed; then she recovered her voice, and returned to her normal state; for this reason I say that in the operation of the epiglottis one should have no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cysts in the throat are called "throat hernias," and they are large abscesses with a color similar to a arrow, and they occur mostly in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental; or naturally, it has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type is according to two manners: one seems like fat, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it is not advisable to make any cuts unless it is a small one, and test and examine all access points: if you find it just like fat and it cannot be moved in any way, treat it as you would treat a nose, and remove it completely if necessary, and wrap it well, and cure it properly until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways in which we can suffer, and I will describe all their similarities; now it is necessary for me to explain the entire distinction between health and disease.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that disease is characterized by heat and fever, as long as the ebullition (boiling) has not passed and the putrefaction (decomposition) is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With no disease, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains satisfaction (comfort), which is its own cure, and according to the state of the body, and begins like a mass, and becomes enlarged; and they are similar in two ways, either greasy or moist, and have a great deal of color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to treat someone with a new injury, test and inquire about all the tools called "instrument" according to their form, as described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of questioning abscesses is to press more or less moistly on the abscess you find, and gradually move your fingers in and out, until you know that the instrument has reached the core; then, according to the size of the abscess, extract the instrument, but be careful not to cause further harm.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture is running from the cut, what color it has, then do as I said for other abscesses; and if the instrument does not bring out moisture, know that it is filled with pus, so make a cross over it, and hold it as pincers, gently peeling it from each side until you expose the core where you treat it with new care; and if you cannot clean it, then remove it in pieces so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains in place, the pain returns many times over; and if it stays for a little while without causing great distress, the wound uses some corrosive powders or hot water, constricts the wound, applies cool things to relieve it, and treats it with other remedies until it heals; but if we cut both sides of the wound, then we cure the cause that generates it.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pain beats against you or causes any other hindrance, act quickly and apply the powder of vitriol, leave it for two or three days until the wound purifies itself and the inflammation of blood subsides; then return to covering what has been affected by the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments that enter, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and they too are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, to enclose fistula abscesses; and they are also like needles with which sorcerers sew, and are made of golden or silver steel, but those that are yellow are more suitable for enclosing the fistulas' cores; and they are likewise of three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the extent of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and if there are hooks with two prongs, they also have three types; and if there are hooks with three prongs, they too are of three kinds; and there are also hooks with one prong, and these are also of three sizes; all of these are necessary for their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tip of these instruments is sharp, and there are some that do not cut well from both sides, which tear the skin, so as not to sever the vein or nerve; and these inserments are knives with edges in multiples, so that the patient does not feel them when opening the abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they should only be used on fleshy parts like legs, arms, breasts, wounds, and similar places; and never make a smaller instrument resembling the cuts of fists, according to this form, with which one stops the blood flow.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in a place that heals the cutting of veins, and arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflame the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like a woman's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and anyone who wants to cure them should do so according to this form from this line b to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicinal herbs with charcoal to the wound, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it is healthy; and if the breast turns downward and becomes soft because of its size, just as it does in women, making them appear as if they have two ribs above, through these similar openings; so that one rib holds the other at the end of each, so that the largest line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b to g. Then scrape off the leather between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and anything necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not complete because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive poultice and leave it until it absorbs the fat and moisture, then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses under the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses under the armpits that present as hard scrofulous nodules or with scales, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B to line G.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, apply clean cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and continue with appropriate treatment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, they should treat it as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound gapes, apply cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery ruptures and the flesh above it severs, it often leads to abscesses, and likewise occurs in a swollen vein with an abscess; and if one recognizes this as due to an arterial rupture, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it at your extremities, you feel a strange sensation; and in the case of a vein, there is a sudden, bright appearance; and it is foolish to try to treat this abscess, especially when it is detached from the muscle, under the skin, with arrows or any other limb, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should seek iron cautery, and he who is in charge should also beware, and on him who has an artery flare up, cut through the skin from above; then make an incision as you've done before, and carefully remove the artery, leaving a double thread of two leagues, just as I've taught you for the removal of the two arteries in the temples; then mark with a probe the area between the two threads until nothing is left there, and release the abscess; then administer the treatment that seems best while the wound is bleeding; then tend to any further dressing needed until it's healed; and if an abscess forms again due to the size of the vein, hold your hand over it, and insert the needle from below into the area you're holding in your hand, piercing it, and leaving a double thread so that you can pull it from the other side; then secure the abscess as I've instructed, or tie it off with one of the threads to either side of the abscess; and if you doubt that the threads have left, insert another needle through all the abscess below the first incision, and tighten the threads in four leagues; then cut away the excess, cut away the excess skin around the wound, and leave what is firmly attached; then place a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, and continue treatments with bandages and dressings until it's healed.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscess of the nail bed
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come from arteries and veins, so too do they occur in the nail bed when it is injured or subjected to excessive strain, and similar conditions.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And these conditions occur more frequently in joints and limbs where there are many articulations, which is a great cause of abscesses, and their appearance resembles the color of the flesh, and they take various shapes with much pain; and when they are squeezed, the patient feels pain, and it is not perfectly whole like the heart, but beneath the heart; and it moves well from all sides, neither going forward nor backward, nor above or below, and a joint that is affected should not be bound up with iron, for fear of causing contraction; and the one located at the head or forehead causes the skin to puss.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it can be gripped with tweezers, cut it at its base; and if it is large, hang it on a hook, peel off the skin, then remove the flesh, and sew up the wound, and apply the cure until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Des grosses boces pendans" translates to "hanging large mouths" in
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It never appears in the stomachs and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" due to its outward appearance, and it has subtle roots, large droppings; and there are both small and very large ones; and I have seen people who had two or more funguses in their bellies that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had a thin root, were constantly moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I collected them and found one weighing XVIII ounces and the other VI Z., and the work of incision is such that if you watch the patient, their moisture is visible, and the color of the articulus is white and moist with a delicate root; if it sticks to the spatula, have the fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting occurs, many serious consequences from blood loss can result, and if you are without help, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient fearful and anxious about the incision, take a well-made plug of silk thread, and bind the articulus as we have said, leaving it for two days; then restrain it, and do not cease to pull the plug of silk thread until it detaches the articulus without effort; and if the roots are thick, be cautious especially when cutting near the belly, but you can still cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not recur; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tissue which is dark in color and poor in quality and full of pus.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enlarged abscess, and I will come to the treatment of this ulcer later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the wound is due to cauterization from a wound or cut from a stone, and it is located on the belly and not in any of the bowels, as it happens with other ruptures, or ulcer that cuts veins or arteries according to what is above, or intestinal gas; and if it is through the rupture of the stone and through the emission of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a slight thing without pain, and has various openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the intestines, then it is more diverse, and when you press it with your fingers, it recovers and then returns, and perhaps it becomes squeezed, greatly constricting the entrance to the bath or through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and opens well when you press it with your hand, not constricting; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: large and hard abscesses, and are inserted according to quantity; and if it is due to wind, it feels soft to the touch, and the pains appear as if it were blood from an artery, or a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, both for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if there is a sign of it in the intestine or bowels, you must instruct the patient to keep still and stretch out straight; then make an incision around the entire edge of the abscess; then command them to wiggle their body slowly between your hands; then extend half of the abscess over the ligament that you have tied; then tie it firmly with a strong thread or piece of strong silk; and open the other half of the abscess which is stretched on the ligament, and insert your finger and extract the intestine; if you find it caught in the ligament, untie it and bring out the intestine towards the outside of the abdomen; and if you find the bowels, cut them at the hilt, and remove the excess; and if the artery or vein is against you, go gently around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert them where you made the incision; then stretch the abscess three times over the needles, and if you see it heal, remove the needles, and leave the ligament until it heals; and cut off the dead flesh by yourself when it becomes soft and ready, and finish the abscess as we have said; then drain the blood or moisture that you find, and treat the wound accordingly, and close up the abscess.
dou chancre	A cancerous wound
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the previous section the signs of cancer, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how to avoid iron treatment; we say that cancer begins in the marris (groin area) and requires great caution in its cure, and advise the ancients that when a cancer is located where it can be cut out, as in the breast, or the thigh, or similar areas, it should all be removed at the beginning; but when it is large and old, one must not even approach it, for I never was able to heal any, nor has anyone ever been healed from it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the work, when the cancer is located where it can be removed, as we have said, do not at any time remove the patient's dark blood; then make the patient well if there is a clear repletion, and operate on the cancer in the best location to perform the operation; then wash all around the tumor or ulcer, and cut from all sides without leaving anything, and let the blood flow out completely, and examine the wound with your hand or any tool, and if the bleeding continues after cauterizing, be careful not to incise the artery or vein, and treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropsis
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the signs of hydrops and in what way the accumulation of water is formed, as well as the symptoms of each condition, and the treatment using medicines, and that which is treated with iron; these should be understood separately. And one must not use iron on these two conditions: namely, tympanitis and yposcare, for they are fatal. Therefore, when treating this hydrops condition, which is called 'eclites' from medications, and the cure does not benefit the patient, consider if the patient is weak or has another illness in addition to hydrops, such as a stomach ulcer or similar; in that case, do not use iron, for there is doubt. And if you see the patient has strong vitality and suffers only from hydrops without any other illnesses, and is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lay the patient gently on your hands, and the minister should press the abdomen while directing the water to the lowest part of the illness, then take the sharp spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Push it in deeply, but do not go so far that it reaches the intestines when inserted, and do not break it. Then observe if there is a drop of blood flowing towards the intestines. You should make your incision three fingers' width directly beneath the armpit, on the left side if the hydrops is from the liver, and on the right if it's from the kidneys; but if it's from the bladder, make the incision wherever it is. Cut through all the skin with your instrument, then squeeze and lift your hand to clear away all the mucus between the skin and the affected area, just as you would when peeling an apple. Then cut the hydrops until the mucus comes out in small drops, which is a sign of the water's root; after that, pull it out and remove this instrument, shaping it as shown:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a fine silver chain, and is made of thin gold or silver, and has a small opening in the middle; on one side, three openings; and two on the other, and one on the other side; and the bone is cut as if with a feather, which is the shape of the incision that scribes make when cutting feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it, there is a hole, so that when the instrument comes into contact with water, it immediately sinks onto the instrument; then you empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is necessary at this time, by chance the patient might die due to the resolution of their spirit from the weapon, or they may lose their palm, or approach death; but you should empty according to the quantity of its virtue and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient suggest, and their pulses. Then remove the instrument and retain the water, which is now held by the core that stops up the hole I mentioned, which you pierce in this manner; then repeat the process with the other side a day later, if you see the patient suffering, and take out a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to force it until only a little water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave them with much water, whether through the cure of a burial or hot sand, or by sweating or a bath or in the sun, and they turn color; and apply drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after draining the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without an opening in the penis, or if the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to pierce through all the subtle spatules according to this form.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then take the subtle opening in the bladder and close it and keep it closed for three or four days, and when the patient wants to urinate, open the closure, allow him to urinate, and then close it again; however, sometimes it is not necessary, because the force of the urine that comes out will not leave the closure.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, it is a gentle closure of the bladder, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in their place are blighted, because no one is born with an opening at the top of the shaft, so they cannot urinate until they raise their shaft high; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach up to the bladder, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method for performing this procedure is that the patient lies on their back, then the head of the shaft and the opening are also as thick as a feather, so that the opening can be made in the right place; and beware of the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops the bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	from the pus of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this illness appears on the penis, and it can be either malicious or benign; you must press them gently with a subtle probe, then cut and clean them all, after which apply a moist cotton in an Egyptian poultice; then continue the healing treatment with a fine linen bandage until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the illness is malicious, with a putrid and foul appearance, it requires cautery treatment.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have it, and if the splint is in a curved state, part of it inside the wound and part outside, then you must first remove the splint that is inside; and when it is hardened, treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, unless the position of the splint is thoroughly secured, blackness and corruption will appear in the splint and bone; then you must remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply a paste made from honey and flour, prepared from red apple bark and leaves, and continue treating with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a blood flow occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery should be performed as follows: if there is a blood flow or corruption, and the part of the member that is corrupt and withdrawn needs to be pushed or guided with a plug, allowing the patient to urinate; when the hair at the top of the member is dry, which happens in those who have not been circumcised, and it develops into a wound or abscess, then you should scrape it with a sharp instrument until the ties are released and the part attached to the member is freed from all sides; if devising this is difficult, you should scrape it gently with a spatula at the top of the member and the stone, then carefully separate them and cover it immediately with a fine cloth dampened with cold water so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	from circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and lightest work for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and elders who performed circumcision around that time, and they did it with force, and all in a hurry; it was the custom because there were two layers, and by chance if one is cut off above, the other below remains intact.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	He returns the cover, and the pain is doubled, and the point of the member is not assured during washing, and sometimes the nail washes away the iron, and it corrupts the work, and often they heal like that without needing washing.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the washing done with force on all the links of thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut precisely from above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if the thread cuts evenly in all directions; but the thread should be tightly twisted around the skin; and it is the first task to make the child understand, if he listens, that you are not doing anything but twisting the thread around the stick as gently as possible, then making him squirm in every way you can. Then twist it between your hands straight, and press the forces between your hands or at the bottom of your feet so the infant does not see, nor any of the tools; then bring your hand back to the stick and blow on its heart, and pull it up as high as the thread on the stick is; then thoroughly wash it from the dirt that has collected on it, then tie the place with a double thread, and attach it between two other threads; and hold it in the second place at the index finger and thumb, and cut through the two threads, then lift the heart up gently. Leave the blood to flow little by little, because this is healing; and apply powder on top and cover it with a piece of gluey dough made from a half-boiled egg mixed with rose water, good oil, and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with other remedies as needed until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of cleansing is thus: both shoulders should be held taut and cut, and the bones should also be as long as the rest equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleansing occurs when the veins are cut and bleed; then you should hold it with your thumb, so that the blood does not run; and do the same for both sides, and if you cannot hold it with your thumb, use tweezers and then finish the procedure.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for three days, and the skin under the arrowhead is swollen, leave it until the abscess is calmed down, and gently peel away the scabs; continue to treat it as best as you can, and avoid the shaft's area, which will do no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the wound suddenly caused by a powder, which we have spoken of in treating powders, and if one takes too much heart, it will go above, so it will not harm; treat it, therefore, as we have said, while it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or a stillborn child, or similar conditions, as we have said in the previous division. If the urine cannot be released and you see that the retention is due to a stone in the bladder or neck, then the patient should be made to bend over his knees; he should lie with pressure on his back and his belly extended upwards from the lower part of his back. This constricts the neck of the bladder towards the stone above, allowing the urine to flow out. If, however, as we have said, the urine does not come out and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction to all instruments called 'syringes', which have this shape: they should be made of fine, light silver, like a bird's feather; their length should be about three and a half palm spans, and they should be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of urination is as follows: take a double thread and tie it to the top of a wool or cotton ball, then insert the thread into the urethra; cut off the excess wool and insert it just below the urethra's opening, then anoint the urethra with oil or butter and egg white, and place the patient on a seat. Elevate the bladder and the urethra with moist oil and olive oil and still water; then gently insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches the root of the organ, then double the urethra over itself towards the opening. Insert the syringe again before the bladder, and have the patient feel the urine flowing until the empty thing is reached; this should not be done haphazardly because the direction in which the thread is placed determines its outcome. Then cut the thread through all the wool bits, and the urine will follow the thread out, then pull it out gently and let the urine flow; repeat the process with the syringe until the bladder is empty, and comfort the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	From the diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcerations or abscesses come to the bladder, and putrefaction is gathered there, you should draw off water and medicines through a device called a "clepsydra", and it is made in this form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; and the cheved (noisy) level of the medicine should be such that it numbs the penis without addition, if one can drain the moisture and push when necessary. And when you pour your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the syringe in the moisture and draw out what is inside; then turn the syringe upside down and squeeze firmly until the moisture enters the syringe. Now pour it immediately into the bladder so that the patient feels it; this is the form of a delicate enema by which one enemas the bladder: thus.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the joint is higher; then open the chest from the side where the ribs split; take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you intend to use for enema; wrap it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the moisture over fire. Then insert the head of the enema into the opening, and squeeze your hand around the bladder until all the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle of it, and perforate it roundly; then thread a strong string through these holes, and assemble the circle like a doll, and put inside what you intend to use of oil and moisture and water, and secure it with the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the methods for dealing with stones and their extraction, along with various medicines; I have explained the distinction between stones that cause rain and all the signs, and which types of stones require surgical intervention; and concerning the bladder and urethra, I will now clearly and concisely tell you.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is trapped in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign of acute bladder infection, similar to water in its subtlety; it opens the way for the patient to urinate, greatly relieving them, often many times, and then it becomes difficult; and much of this discharge comes from the foundations. The treatment for children up to four years old is light, but it is much more challenging for the elderly, those between youth and old age; the cure is lighter for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a enema, to draw out all the impurities from the bowels.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often becomes trapped, seeking to pass the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and straighten them, and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, without moving back up; then place the patient's hands between his legs, with his hands on his thighs, so that the bladder inclines downwards; then press and touch inside. If you feel the stone in a particular spot, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out at the touch from anywhere, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and if the patient is older, use your middle finger; press it deeply into its foundation, grasp the stone, and when you feel it on your right side, close the bladder's neck; then press down on your right side, and push the stone out towards the opening where you see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the practitioner to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch his right hand upwards with the fingers, and with his left hand, remove the skin covering the stones in the area where the cutting is done; then use the forceps, which take on this shape.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make an incision between what is between the buttocks and the fundament, not too deep but on the side of the left thigh; and it should be straight on the stone, and both legs should be placed as if on a foundation, and the scar should be wide on one side and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; so that the pressure from the leg which is on the fundament, makes it come out without effort; and know that there are stones with angles and margins: then it is easy to extract; and if it is below, like a gland, round, and smooth, whose passage is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you need to extract it with pliers which are also like a file at the top, so that you can extract the stone without it escaping; or you insert a very thin curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot do this, you enlarge the opening slightly, and if it is covered, extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, first pull out the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, they must cut it out carefully, making a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: he dies, or his urine flows again through the wound that the limbs cannot heal; but nevertheless, strive hard to extract it with pincers, as you remove it piece by piece, and when you have completed your work, dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and tighten it, and place a damp cloth of oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then wrap the patient in a woolen bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of oil and water arises from the place, then apply the treatment with ointment of dye and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosion come to the wound, and collections of blood in the bladder, and it retains urine, which is known in this manner as if there were no urination: then press your finger into the wound, extract the pus, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause illness; then cleanse the wound with water and leach and salt, and aid it in every way that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that at all times when you treat it, you bind both thighs together, and apply medicines to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it is passed through the urethra, stuck together, and urine cannot pass; then if you treat this as I say, cutting many times, one may excuse the cutting because of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested it this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the beginning according to this form, and place it at three angles into the fire:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra away from the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently pull the iron towards the stone until it reaches it; and return the iron to your hand in and out of the stone, as much as you can pierce the stone from another side; soon enough, urine will come out, then press your hand on the part remaining of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is often broken and jumps out with urine, and scratches the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that defends it, then pull the stone from below and another from above, then make a stick to pierce the stone between the two edges, then pull it out forcefully, loosen the knot, and cleanse the frozen blood in the wound; and cure it as long as it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the woman's stone" (referring to kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare for a stone to occur in women, and if it does, the cure is difficult, and it is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that it is not possible to find a woman well-versed who knows how to uncover herself, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of healing; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman's body is harder than that of a man, so it needs to be cut deeper, and great fear exists. And if necessary, it is fitting to command a mistress well-knowing in this matter, and seek her out diligently, and if you do not find one, there is no need for excessive subtlety; present her with a simple task in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and instruct her to perform what you command regarding the examination of the stone; and take great care that this woman is chaste: then she must push down her index finger into the base and seek for the stone. And if she finds it, she should press it down firmly on the patient's left hand over the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she has a stone, it is necessary to move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to the thigh, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle part, where it moves, and feel the stone in that area; and do not move her leg either above or below the stone, and make the first incision on her hip small. Then bend her right to the hip, if you feel the stone so deeply in the wound that the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know these things to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood does not cease to flow, put vitriol on the wound and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work while the stone is still hard, and have tools that I told you for removing stones from men to aid you in your task; and if the blood continues to flow, and it is an artery cut, place powder on the wound and strain it with cloth and bandages, and do not repeat this, leaving the stone and not pulling it out unless by chance the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the eyes open, return to your work while the stone is still hard.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carneous
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rameous aqueous is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white soft tissue, which is detached from the heart of the animals, containing the egg; and it is called "soft tissue," and never properly part of the egg's membrane if one believes it to be another organ; and this is the smooth skin of the testicle between the white soft tissue that we have mentioned; and this does not happen spontaneously.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rameous is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and this material expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from a percussion on the joints, and this moisture takes many forms: either a jaundice, or without red, or black, or white water, and so forth; and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white as we have said, the abscesses are bright, long in shape like an arrow, and do not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the membrane itself, the abscesses are bright with a part of the arrow's tip, and for this reason one thinks it is another arrow; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white as we have said, it smells well; then when you want to know the color of the moisture, test all the affected area as mentioned above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.
