And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his strength and the fulfillment of his body; then lay him on his back, on something slightly elevated, and place several sheets under him; then sit him up on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the staff to one of the two ribs near the heart of the chest; then take the scalpel, and cut the skin of the chest from the long end to the elbow, and make the incision completely straight by cutting the skin of the chest up to the satisfaction of the white flesh, and carefully scrape it according to the tom strength; then pierce the flesh with water in a wide opening, and extract all the water, and then put your stitches, and pull the flesh upwards; do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the flesh; cut it as carefully as possible, or else the water will return; and if the wound is successfully closed, bring him back to his original position when you have finished with the flesh. Then sew together the two books of the chest ribs with a stitch, and treat it like other wounds until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspended, in doubt about the discharge of blood; then cut the vein from the entire suspension, and extract the heart, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the blood is gathered in two parts together, knowing that these are two branches; cut off the other part just as you did with the first one equally, then wipe away the blood, and apply a clean moistened cloth with rose oil to the wound; and place another moistened cloth with wine and oil on top, and put two bandages over it, and secure it with all the bindings according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and make them of shredded wool according to this form, and join them together with stitching at the gusset of the breeches; one of them should be sewed close to the root as far as the back, and the other on the side near the elbow; and the third across both shoulders, and tighten it in the loop of the braies. Never use this cautery with a metal blade, but rather a small, sharp one, cut through the skin, and expose the white substance that contains water; if you take the cautery in this way, pierce the syph (supposedly a type of growth or lesion) as before, and burn it with this hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup should be used in all ways that you can, as long as it is completely drained; and beware that the fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is safer; and move gently to avoid blood clots, and take care with the operations of cutting; and if anything goes against you, whether it is a complication from an abscess or another issue, then treat what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this operation because of its horror, then apply perforation as I have told you, and make sure that when you are certain by the signs that we have mentioned that the inflammation has subsided, place the patient in a high position; then incise the abscess at the base, into the deep part of the wound, and open it widely so that all the pus can flow out. Then cover it with cotton and bandage it, allowing the remaining pus to drain. Then dress the wound until the infection is healed; and if a white cloth does not allow the pus to escape from the wound, you should insert a quill or the instrument used to draw off the water from dropsical patients, as has been described before. Open the wound wider, and know that the pus will return and collect again after six months or so, and when it collects as before, the patient's condition will improve.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the hair follicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Knowing that in this branch there are many more dangers, I seem to think it is better to leave it; and I will tell you about the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come where there are hair follicles; and most often they occur in the skin; this is due to many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is due to excessive acidity and bitterness that spreads to the hair follicles, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the skin; it does not cause pain, and it is a deep abscess; sometimes there are several painful and black abscesses, or with a greenish hue, and they never come from a new artery, or from swelling in a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, if it is known by the hot condition of an abscess at its top, when you press it with your fingers; and it is not proper that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	What is made from vein inflation is known by its disposition to the sensitive expression of the fingers, and it can be well cut along this model, and along other parts; and it is that you remove the heart of the lumps, then the heat is above, and the trail is strong and white, and releases the suspension from all parts of the heat.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the heat is already hard with these cuts, then it is necessary that you remove the heat and cut it; and if it is too hot, or in those who are inside the vessels, it is necessary that you release all that tension, and cut it properly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the source of the pain is behind, it is necessary that you remove it entirely, and extract the foreign body, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, immediately apply a moist woolen compress with rose oil and wine to the wound, then use other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess surrounded by a covering similar to a boil, with the testicles becoming swollen and painful; it causes the patient great distress. The treatment for this disease is just as delicate as the one mentioned before, and we will tell you about its procedure according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You should let the patient rest on a clean bed, then hang the suspending bands of the veins below your hands, to all the vessels close to the wound, and draw them taut; then cut with a sharp spatula across the vessels while they are exposed, and strip away from each side, as we have said in extracting arteries within temples. Then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first joint where the vein appeared, and tie it again to the other end; then cut them straight through, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture. Treat the wound as you would others, so that no vessel leaks, because if they do not bleed, all vessels will gain strength, and it is necessary to draw the veins from all vessels, so that the eye does not lose its nourishment due to vein incision, and dries up and cannot help itself.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sinew.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The symptoms of this condition occur through the rupture either from the section (surgery) that causes it, or from an extension in the abdomen in the region of the angles, which makes the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the openings; and this rupture is either due to the surgery itself, or from the extension of the sinew, and these two ways have similar causes: a blow, a fall, straining, lifting a heavy weight, and similar actions; and the signs when it's due to an extension of the sinew are that it occurs gradually over time and not suddenly, and the abscess is even until near its end, because the rupture (surgery) pushes on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is from the incision that a sudden pain arises at the beginning, and various abscesses appear under the skin close to it, due to the discharge of the intestine and the flow of blood from the syphilis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never remove the pus with the intestine, as it becomes stuck and causes great pain for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these poor treatments with iron, for which one must be wary.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method for this procedure is that you command the patient to straighten the intestine in his hand inside the wound if it can be done; then remember on his collarbone between your hands and ease the hips; then spread the heart on top, and shave all the flesh from the bones until the white flesh becomes exposed from all sides. Then insert your index finger after the bone, between the white flesh that is under the skin of the thigh, and between the second flesh, and remove what is behind the bone, and between the second flesh; then move your right hand inside the heart of the flesh, and place the white flesh on top with your left hand, and ease the bone towards the tailbone; and command the assistant to stretch the bone upwards and loosen what is attached behind the membrane. And be careful if there is no intestine wrapped or hard white flesh, and if you find anything, insert it into the belly below the skin. Then take a needle with a thick thread of four threads, and insert it in the back part of the white flesh after the skin of the thigh; then cut the testicles that appear from the threads until there are three threads remaining; then intertwine them one on top of the other like a cross, and tie the white flesh which we mentioned is under the skin of the thigh with a strong thread of two parts. Then wrap the testicles with the thread, and tie them together so that no vessels that nourish them can enter, and the abscess does not form again; then attach the first long thread of two parts to this one, and after these two threads, leave the white flesh under the heart of the thigh a finger's length; then do the rest according to the roundness of the bone. Then cut the part that is under the skin of the thigh as we mentioned before; then apply moist wool to the wound, and attach the thread as we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white flesh we have mentioned, after incision, out of fear of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, leaving the wound open until it heals on its own; and if it takes time to heal, then apply hot water as we have mentioned, until it heals completely; then treat the wound with other remedies, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh herniation
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, never has anyone dared to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like the root of a tree which is assembled with a joint, in such a way as you bind vessels after cutting them slightly from below; then cut through it and treat the abscess of him who opens, until the vessels stop bleeding; and cure it as we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur without the opening of the vessels, as we have said, and it should not drain any intestines; if it does, it is a little thing, and one should watch every hour. Nevertheless, if it persists too long at this point, one believes it to be a wound or a abscess, as long as the intestines are drained; and this occurs due to the expansion of the abscess at the angle, as we have said, because it expands then becomes soft and swollen, opening the vessels; and its cure is through cautery, as we have previously mentioned; and never should it be cured in this way with iron. And so, the patient lies on his back, with his hands under him, then cut the vessel of the rupture with a sharp knife according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the abscess located beneath the skin, take the blade, and place it onto the exposed part of the abscess; press firmly into the abdomen, cut the two exposed parts of the abscess on top of the blade, and pull one way, then the other. Then remove the blade, and do not cover or extend the wound in any way, as I have told you in the cure for the vessel of intestines; and then treat it with a cure for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they are dirty and the injury is clean, then do so until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the rupture, but the cauterization moves in this place, and is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the thick skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the testicles is often softened in many men because the substances inside are mollified, and it becomes visible. When one wishes to treat it, they must lay the patient on his back and cut the softened skin close to the natural skin; then bring the two edges together with a single stitch or, if necessary, several firm stitches; subsequently, cut between the stitches and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, ensuring not to let any thread remain.
dou chastrement	1. This treatise, a guide for medical practices, offers
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Although castration is prohibited by our laws, I would not mention it in this book; however, it is necessary to discuss it in two ways: one is that you respond wisely when asked about it and provide a wise cure; the other is because we often need to perform castration on certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cats, and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say, therefore, that castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one we perform by attraction, make the animal sit in hot water until the joints are softened and relaxed; then press them with your hand until they are healed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	On castration of the penis: it is necessary that you tie up the animal and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then fasten the suspensory, and make cuts on each side at the base of the penis, as much as to thoroughly cut; and leave no drop of blood, nor any subtle blood which lies on the veins; and this method of castration is superior to that which is done by attraction, because in attraction there may remain something from the joints, which causes the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is in two ways like men: one is when between the two sexes, it appears as the figure of a woman's nature, with hair and never cuts urine short.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, who have a penis on their hand, as if it were a phallus, and two vulvas.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is to clean the affected parts carefully and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for those whose urine flows through the skin of the penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tendon
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tendons are a tight tissue attached to the natural part [of the body], as long as it is too ugly to see; and no woman has ever had one so strong as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should remove the excess of tendons from your hand or fingers, and cut them lightly; do not cut too deeply, lest complications from blood loss occur, then treat it with another cure until it is healed; and for another condition that appears at the mouth of the wound, and spreads, and perhaps jumps, and resembles a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to take care of it, as we have said before, with the tweezers and cure as long as it is healthy.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of a woman is not properly understood, or the opening (vagina) is small; it is either by birth or an accident that occurs due to illness, or it is because of improper adjustment, or some subtle and specific condition, and it affects childbirth or, sometimes, the flowers (breast milk), and one must consider all these things carefully.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the dislocation is recently apparent, whether by your own hand or by chance.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle dislocation, and it is recently apparent near the joints, act quickly: place your two index fingers together, and have the patient lie on their back with their legs spread; then form both joints into a rounded shape until the subtle dislocation is corrected and the joint is stable. Then take wool, moisten it in oil, and apply it to the affected area, having the patient lie on their stomach each day so they cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the dislocation is hard and deep, then you should use a spatula-like instrument resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from heat, suspend it with a splint and compress; have the medicines that stop blood flow, such as witch hazel, dragon's blood, incense, in abundance; then apply a broad poultice so that the wound cannot close; and thus keep it for a long time, and then apply a dry linen bandage; and continue other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the swelling comes from heat, if it needs to be covered, do so according to this manner; if it is not an abscess, apply compresses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess swollen from heat, do not apply any treatment with the hand.
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without usual care, become enlarged and hardened; in the discussion I have previously mentioned the appearance and signs of old hemorrhoids, and I will now describe those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are completely in the rectum, and do not appear to be felt, can only be effectively treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the rectum can be felt, and these are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then stretch her limbs with pincers, and compress them at their roots, then sprinkle medicinal powders to stop blood, such as lime and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and when blood comes, let it stand in a decoction of sumac and bark from pomegranates and gall and similar things, and then take flour from barley, and mix it with honey and wax, and make an emplaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it becomes moist, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If no, then make suction cups rise on the back and on the breasts without hurting; then take cloth, and dampen it in plantain juice or in holly juice with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, continue the treatment with the wound dressing as long as it remains clean; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a raw head, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text; then cure the wound as long as it is clean.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in women
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many different types of abscesses occur in the body, such as chancre, previous abscesses, herbs, boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, it is necessary for me to discuss in this treatment the hot abscess that occurs in the body, which is not like other abscesses that discharge pus; and if you are skilled in the work of fire, pay attention to whether the abscesses become red in their initial stage, filled with heat and fever, and turn red as you can see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not hurry to pierce, but let the patient suffer the pain until it is eased; then place the patient in a reclined position with two small pillows under his legs, and have him rest on his back with his feet extended away from the leg that is being treated. Spread the patient's knees apart, place his arms below his knees, and secure them tightly with a good bandage; then suck air from the patient's right side and insert the tool used to open the abscess, which will determine the shape of the opening afterward. Ensure when you insert the tool that it goes as deep as necessary so that no part of the tool enters beyond the required depth, potentially harming the patient; if the tool is too large, cover the deepest part of the abscess with cloth to prevent the tool from causing discomfort. Place the end of the tool above the opening and secure the tool.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and they make an incision with a gentle hand, if it is necessary to cover the opening, take a spatula; and when the bowel is emptied, it is necessary to put moist tents in rose oil or in dry green oil into the wound, all around the margin, and put outside on the margin and on the lateral finger clean moistened water with cooked alder leaves or mullein; then cure after two days of treatment until it is healed; and never raise the margin and the wound by a water enema and honey, and then water or cooked lily roots and long aristology; then return to treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the margin, it is necessary to be careful not to use fire, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	from childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Skill is first in the dance, that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and its signs are when you see the woman straining down, and desiring to push: then hasten the child to emerge; then know that these children are according to nature's figure, and follow their chief, and second him with them; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends onto his head, he follows him with it, and the mother gives birth to her excesses through good purification; and this one who does not come otherwise, does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes upon its own feet, but rather affects the body where it touches, whether on the hands or the feet, or on the belly, or sometimes turns around by chance onto its neck, and assumes other bad shapes; so it is necessary for the physician to be wise and subtle in these matters, to ward off errors and misunderstandings, and I will show you all the forms of how to aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fever comes upon the head from a natural cause, and the woman is giving birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then she should be placed on a bed or held by other women; and one should prepare an oil or fennel mixture, as described below, and then apply the ball between her two fingers, of which the shape is like this:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut open the second [area], and dig into his fingernail as deep as the moisture that is inside; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clean the woman with fennel seed musk with sesame oil; then make her sneeze and blow her nose from a cold condition, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If both hands are unable to insert, it is necessary that you gently re-align them little by little; and if they still cannot enter, place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet upwards; then remove the seat to the ground, and turn off the woman so she does not try to stand up; and if her hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, cut through the hand that is placed in front, extract the child, and realign it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on its feet, it needs to be pushed up; then it returns little by little until it is even; then press on the feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it can jump up to its hocks, with the command to press, and it makes a sneeze of relief; if it jumps further, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, if it returns little by little, according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come as we have said, take a little musk, and oil of rose, and gum resin, and grind them all in a mortar; then apply this remedy to the female nature both inside and outside, and let her lie in warm water down to the ribs; when she is moistened, make a collar of myrrh and place it around her, leaving it for an hour. Then have her sit, then make her sneeze, press her mouth and nose, and gently massage her belly, for the child is now ready to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the emergence of the child onto its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child presents in this position, he should gently move his hands; then place himself on his collarbone, and let his feet hang down, lying on his side; and gradually move his hands, first pressing them onto his stomach, then lifting them up, and moving his feet; and when the child does not struggle, take hold of his feet and move them, then his stomach upwards, and finally turn his hands; and gently rock the child; and instruct the woman to press herself down as long as the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her down on a bed and straighten her legs; then apply the musclyg (a term of unknown modern equivalent) that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, sit her in a position to bring back the hand; and carefully deliver the child according to its natural form, make her sneeze, and instruct her to press as the baby is delivered.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of the child on its mother's womb, let it spread its hands and turn its face away from its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I know that the hand has its own motion, turning little by little and gently; and when it is steady, apply a light, muscly, oily compress from above, as we have said, then command it to move little by little; and once you have done this, place it on a warm seat and order it to press; and make the patient sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the rest
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner of treatment, do the following at once: if the moistors (swelling) is still present, press it with your thumb until it's emptied; then place the affected part on its face and neck, ensuring it's not restrained, and let the child breathe until you've positioned him correctly, as is appropriate, and instruct the woman to lie down at times.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born many times, and never more than three or four at a time; this is not strange, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are strange things, and they do not live long, nor do they have a name; I know that they multiply, and are caused by the pleasure which devises them, which is tied to desire; and they never appear as naturally as others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they appear badly, if the cure is as we have said, and there are subtle pains, making it suddenly and lightly do what it does, and act thus as it should be moved for healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No joints are formed in the body I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child according to the measure of his glorious wisdom, and it is necessary that the skilled surgeon knows this well, for sometimes a similar thing happens; he must act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman who has lost her child in the womb, as I mentioned in the previous division, and there is no sign of delivery, and you are forced to use manual assistance; it is necessary that you know if the woman's health is good and does not have any fear or worry about death. The woman should be placed on her back, and her legs should be inclined downward and raised; the midwife should assist in this process from two sides, so she is not disturbed by removing the child. Then, wet your fingers with moist oil mixed with althae and fenugreek powder and flaxseed, and apply this to the woman's hands and between her fingers. Gently massage it inside the vagina, then insert a finger (or a tool) at a slight angle where the cervix should be, and check if the baby is positioned correctly for delivery. If so, gently but firmly push on the abdomen below the belly button towards the lower back, and apply pressure to the sides of the pelvis; this will help guide the baby down. Be careful not to insert the finger or instrument too far, and ensure it is comfortable for the woman. The shape of the cervix is like a ring.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another joint, where you need it most, so that the extraction is even; and then continue to move it equally from one side to the other to help it pop out, and the dislocation will be healed just like this:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains stuck, apply no oil to any of its joints, but press it into that part and pull the other part; and if nothing comes out, then place this dislocation higher up on the limb and continue until it pops out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward before the other and cannot return due to tightness, it is necessary that you wrap it with a cloth until it pops out completely; then cut at the joint of the finger or the thumb, and do the same for the other hand, and for the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and stuck in the birth canal, and has a sharp point assembled, you should insert the spiny spatula between your fingers, and press and extract the head; or use the instrument called "almidach" to shape it with the tools of this chapter that follow; and thus also perform on infants with a large natural head. Then pull the bones out with pincers, and if the head gets stuck, cut it in pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, pierce it until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infant is on its feet, there is a slight attraction, and the direction towards the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is twisted in the belly or the bowels, it is necessary to pull it out from under the wrapping on the hand; and making an incision in the belly or bowels, until the moisture that is there is corrected; and if another member is broken and remains stuck, and the pain comes back, he should press his hand into the opening of the wound; then he should make an incision or two, and pull it out; and if the opening of the wound has narrowed due to heat from an abscess that formed there, it is not appropriate to work on it, but rather it is necessary to apply moist and greasy things; and administer poultices, and use water that softens and moistens.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the hernia is on his side, and you can make it even, apply what we have said for a live child; and if there is no possibility of removing it in one piece, then leave nothing from the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, then apply what we have said concerning the abscesses that come from the vein; and if bleeding occurs, place it in strong restraint, and apply other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had been bitten by a child; then I examined another on that same spot, and removed the other bite.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, a painful abscess formed in her cheek, swelling so much that it opened, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong plaster, and an egg came out, and after some days, others.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because that stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound, and handled the bone as best I could, until the woman was in a better state; and she remained in that position for a long time, and then took a little bow of light; and I have never remembered this chapter to be useful except when a master encounters something strange and knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	return the woman to her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of the press, with which books are bound; and at its turn to the other side, it goes back to the two limbs of the binding.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; and the mouth opening should be wide enough, with a margin measuring one palm and a half in length; and both sides of this same wood should have a fitting adjustment, either half a palm long or slightly more; and this fitting is placed within the mare's mouth to open it when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or box wood, resembling pliers; it should have two adjustments, each one palm long and two fingers wide; when you open the mare's mouth with the entire instrument, make the woman lie down on her back, keep her legs apart, and close the two adjustments together into the mare's mouth. Then, apply pressure to the entire instrument as you did with the pliers, opening the mare's mouth until it reaches its desired width.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all equipped and have many similar appearances; and when the surgeon has arranged them properly, the work is done faster, and it benefits people more due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument even if you have not arranged it properly, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine (a tool used during childbirth) is withdrawn from the mother, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then have her exhale strongly while holding her hands over her mouth and nose; and if she does not suffocate, all is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is not possible, take I a needle and make I an opening or cover, and insert herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calament, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or put in water over the fire. Then place one end of the needle or opening in the mouth of the wound, and hold it there until the vapors enter the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient experiences a second complication.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if, after this treatment, the patient still feels pain, instruct them to moisten their left hand with sesame oil or deer musk and then apply it to the wound. They should hold it there until they feel a second tug; when they do, they should gently press and pull on both sides at once, allowing the wound to heal.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the mare (uterine contraction) is tightly closed, we have said the cure to sneeze and fumigate with herbs; and if it does not respond to all that we have said, be careful not to follow; but whoever is at the mouth of the mare, tie him to the woman's calf, then wash him with a four-ingredient ointment; he will release and return, and leave. However, when she sneezes, a bad odor arises in the stomach and head, and the sick person becomes pale.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is appropriate to use suitable fumigations: no one of the ancients has tried fumigation with parsley and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one cauterizes a woman to stop the flow of blood and milk is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a snake, and the tip is placed finely in the middle, and the base is wide over the fire; and the fumes are on the coals, and the smoke until it is completely consumed, and then another one is started.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not had their foundation pierced, but they have a subtle syphilis: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this syphilis with her finger, and do not use a sharp instrument, and hold the clamp so that she does not touch it; then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, and apply the dressing until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not return, insert or open a plug of flesh, and leave it for a long time, and it becomes rigid when the child wants to move into its chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And suddenly this stopping of the wound or abscess occurs; then it is necessary to cover this stoppage: whether it is cured, as we have said about the plug of flesh.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that originate from beneath the foundation are larger than those that come from above, or there can be more than one fistula; and when this nodulation is old, it opens up, and still emits a white or subtle discharge, and these fistulas do not heal; they are recognized by the fact that there is an emission of pus or air when the patient evacuates, and sometimes they burst.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the ulcers pierce through to the bladder, and through to half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and through the root of the cock.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus, one recognizes the fissure in the fundament, and it is not present; and it is you who inserts your index finger into the fundament and pushes a fine needle of iron or steel into the fissure when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is curvature, and you insert a thin probe or a horsehair as fine as you can feel it with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and it does not cause any expulsion or vomiting, as we have said, know that it will not pierce; be haste in treating it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urethra, if it lets go of the urine, and cannot be healed by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the thigh, then the veins nearby are affected; if there is no twisting or change in the pain around it, and it remains bent, and no medicine or dressing helps, then there is no cure for these persistent fistulas other than hard work and the futile attempts of foolish practitioners.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is neither persistent nor old, there is hope for healing by fire, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on their back between your hands; they bend their legs up to their thighs, and their knees are bent towards their belly. Then insert a thin strip of iron, or a plunger if there is twisting, as long as you know where the vein is located.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner. S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he/she is in such a state, it is good.

Then banish those evil-looking threads that resemble a bird's feather, and do not leave anything.

des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the anus, resembling grains of resin, and ranging from small to large, and causing bleeding; and those that protrude outside, one or more in number, extending from the anus, and also containing blood, having a flesh-like color; and the cure for hemorrhoids within the anus is to command the patient to rest in bed until the anus heals completely and the child is delivered. If urgent, using forceps or your finger, remove them at their base; otherwise, wrap them in cloth or cotton or a piece of chamois, and extract them gently. Cut them off, then apply a powder made from hot spices over the cauterized area; or, as mentioned in the cautery chapter, cauterize them, treating other ailments as well until they heal. If the anus cannot be extracted, administer enema with strong and bitter solutions to wash out what is inside, so that it can come out easily. As for treatment, if the patient experiences pain and their child has already been delivered, the cure is light; press them gently with your finger or forceps, then treat as we have said until they heal, avoiding incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary, you must administer the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread, and wrap it around an needle, then draw the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and pass both ends of the thread under the needle, and if it is too wide, tighten the forming thread, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus with all the rest, leaving one for draining the blood; then place a moist cloth or wax on the base, and put it in place, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until the wound heals, and when it has fallen, apply treatment and other remedies until it is healed.

dou fremit	Douloure" is the Old French word
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice are a small, hairy creature that burrows into the body, and they do so very thoroughly; the wound never freezes, and one feels them as if dead from trembling, spreading throughout the whole body, especially in the hands.

And the cure is that you take a needle from an goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and place this needle on the trembling until it turns red all around; then turn your hand over the whole needle until you cover all around the trembling, and set it in place, and pull out the trembling from its roots.

de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a cloth enema

Never should an enema be made with silver or gold, or with melted lead or iron; and never should these small and large instruments be used according to those to whom they are entrusted.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those are therefore small, used in the treatment of children who are weak and suffering.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	He must prepare a small and wide enema if it is too narrow above; thus, the abdomen is tied according to this manner.
