des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the parts where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the use of stone, and sword and knife, or lance or spear or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the neck, or head, or leg, or belly, or liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is due to stone or similar objects, and the skin is nevertheless torn and the wound deep, and you doubt an abscess forming: do this as soon as possible for the sake of the head itself, especially if there is little blood loss from the wound, and treat it conversely in the affected part; and remove the patient's fullness of wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be healed, let his flesh be reduced and he should not drink wine or eat char; and apply a poultice of rose oil only or of astringent wine; and if there is a hot abscess, apply it to the wound while it is fresh with all its blood, and do not let air, powder, which I will mention later, touch it; and if fire has moved it, apply some ointment as long as it is clean.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like the size of a sword or similar, and the edges cannot come together, they should be brought together by stitching, as I will explain for wounds in the belly from the stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, it bleeds and only lasts for a short time if not treated; then treat the wound with medicine and replace the skin with hard wood, and instruct the patient to eat substantial foods such as roast meat, bread, cooked grain, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrid flesh or rotting leather that does not reach the bone and eats away at it all, drain it thoroughly, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein from which, without cutting, it cannot be stopped with medicine, cut the artery, but if cutting it does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you place this powder that sticks so that the fire moves away.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method of the powder is as follows: take one part frankincense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts of the live charcoal, mix it finely, apply it to the wound, and tighten it until it spreads well and joins all the blood; then bind it tightly and leave it unbound unless it swells, for the medicine should not be removed as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should one use charcoal only, unless you have frankincense or dragon's blood, but the fire must have moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if there is no powder applied; but place on it some well-prepared ointments, or a paste made from water and honey and oats flour, until it becomes soft; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound and it is small, then extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you below about the treatment of these fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the deep wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, then it has no distinction from that in the head, but if there is damage to the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy but to let them heal without applying anything restrictive, as that would harm the nerves and cause them to retreat; do not put any sharp objects on the wound, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member. But apply medicine under, such as washed chalk in sweet water mixed with rose oil, and clean bandages also in sweet water, and other stones according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, if it cuts through the tendons and ligaments, then treat it until it heals.

If the wounds are deep and extensive, with pus and bowels present, then pierce them or cut them deeper; if an artery is severed, and bleeding occurs, disregard it and apply cauterization; if there is a thorn in the throat or the heart, and the flow of blood must be stopped, carefully remove the thorn without touching the throat, and then bandage it according to its natural shape; subsequently, tighten the bandage and do not change it for several days, and treat with remedies until healing occurs; if the wound has pressed into the bone, dig out any pieces of bone you can reach, leaving those you cannot; if the wound is fresh, apply the poultice as mentioned above.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a lance or sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or sword, and deep, then consider the direction of the air in the wound as the patient alone knows: then know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not so deep and still has all its blood, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it for the blood to stop flowing back into the body and causing further harm to the sick person; instead, apply an attractive dressing and change it twice a day. And if you have no dressing, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the sick person sleep on the wound for three, four, or more days; if there is no spasm, no shaking of the body, or any strange feeling, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wound with various remedies and others, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; then treat it accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is shallow or deep, front or back, treat it as follows; if it is large, sew it up; and if small, use powder; and if it affects the bone and has splintered pieces, clean the wound thoroughly if they are unclean, and remove foreign bodies if necessary; and for other wounds in other limbs, judge them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruption of the belly is great and medium and small; from a large wound, no time does the intestine, or the nerve of the intestines, protrude; and stitching is more difficult, and never worth less than the small wound compared to the large one, because one must handle the intestines with more care, not pushing them in too much; for they tend to swell quickly, causing pain, if pushed in too far, and it is better to move the middle wounds, because one must first reset the intestine to its original place before attending to the others. And know that the rupture of the belly has four types of stitches: common stitches in the stomach stitch, and stitches for other wounds on the body, and other specific stitches are common to other wounds; yet they are more suitable with the stomach stitch, and I will explain each one separately.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestine sticks out, and it is a difficult thing to reset, then this is one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth with hot water only, or cook in water with squinant (a type of spice), and cipre (possibly a herb), and spice; then remove the intestine as soon as the swelling is gone; and never use this as a constricting wine, but let it be moved so that it deflates.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestines are filled with hot or cold water and the veins are closed, for this eases the entry of a few things; and if it cannot enter, make a small cut in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first care is to move the limb, that we should not cut without great need; and this is the instrument to split: cut inside the cavity and pull outward, see the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines burst forth, if you can return them to their natural place in their proper position, do so if you have the power, for it is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and located below the stomach, it is necessary to have the patient lie on their back and elevate their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, place the head and breast higher than the lower parts, and pay attention so that the wounded area is higher than the other; thus, you must apply what I said for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, prepare what you need; then take in your hands a gentle, warm remedy to cover the entire wound and gather the edges together; this is the common method of stitching, using one or more needles, according to the size of the wound, leaving two spaces at the head of the wound, and threading a needle with strong, fine thread; pierce the two layers of skin with the two points of the scalpel, which are beneath the skin, until you have pierced it from that part, and gather the two points of the scalpels together four times; then wrap double thread around the needle on both sides, and gather the two edges of the wound neatly together, leaving two spaces, and thread another needle; secure it with thread like the first one, and continue to do this as needed until the entire wound is closed; the needles should be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, for they can pierce all the flesh, but if they are too thick, they cannot enter properly. Therefore, they should be medium; do not pull the needles too far beyond the flesh and skin or they will open up the wound before the stitching is complete; then trim off the ends of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient while sleeping, and place tenting or cloth over the ends of the needles to keep them in place, leaving them until the wound is healed; this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as only one or two stitches are required, and it involves gathering together the two layers of skin and the two points of the scalpel together at a single needle; when you have finished stitching, return to where you began, stitching like one sews a cloth; leave spaces between each stitch about the size of a finger; this method is used for men, and I once stitched a wound on a man who had been stabbed in the belly; it was more than a palm-length wide and extended two palms below his intestines; it was a deep wound.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its original position after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, which was a miracle; and I did not cure him with any treatment, for I was in a place where none could be found, neither any medicine; and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it with honey-water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and hold it to the wrong side of the fabric, puncturing it straight through to the right side; once it has pierced the fabric, bring the needle back up on the wrong side near where you started, and continue stitching in the same way as a leatherworker sews fur, leaving the thread on one side and picking it up on the other until the stitch is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second stitching method, which Galen calls "so as to form," is like a way that nature itself sews together the two parts, applying one of the heads with satisfaction to the other head in this manner: insert a needle or a satisfying head close by, and pierce it only into the flesh, leaving the two heads of the satisfying thing; then turn the needle and pierce it from the opposite part towards this inside, as well as the other two heads of the satisfying thing; and then pierce both from the opposite part to this inside, in the other two heads of the mirach on the other side. This is the moving method of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen calls this method "the two-needle stitching," and no one testifies to it other than the fact that one must sew the stomach with two needles, each having thread; and you should pass one needle from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and be aware that when the rupture is inside the stomach, the stitching is more difficult than for other parts of the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you probe the fresh wound, and all its blood, in such a way that the armpit has moved, then rearrange the internal organs and the flesh; then apply a poultice with char-burning powder, and if the armpit has moved, apply any present dressing, as long as the wound is open; and bind the thread, and make sure the healing is sealed with mirach; then treat the wound like other wounds until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then use a piece of old cotton and move it in the wound twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition to these arrangements for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound is affecting vital members, it is necessary to moisten with light linen cloth dipped in warm or rose oil, and place it around the wound, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction, which often happens, clisterize with black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines. Puncture them inside, and know that when they are the large intestines, healing is easier than for the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal organ, called "young" (or perhaps "innard"), cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the frailty of its vessels, the subtlety of the entire body, and the similarity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the seed (or "zirbe") jumps out of the wound while it is still fresh, similar to how an intestine does, you must reset it immediately; if it has become old and turned white or black, then it's important to tie down the black part to prevent blood loss, as it contains vessels and arteries. Then cut through what's between the ties and hang the two seeds from the bottom of the wound until the seed pops out, facilitating its extraction.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it cannot be restored in any man, as I have seen one nobleman struck by a lance through his belly; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became inflamed and developed into a fistula, from which emerged excretion and flatulence; I treated it according to my ability, and did not cease subtilizing until he was healed, and the wound made whole.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healed, I doubted that the patient would not suffer pain in his belly; but he felt no pain, only improved condition, food, and drink; and certain healers say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated in this manner: take large plasters, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the plaster has opened its mouth, place it over both lips, so that it sticks to them; then cut off the head of the plaster, and hold it in such a way that he cannot untie it, and put another plaster in the same manner as before until the wound is completely healed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That chief is attached to the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and it can be tied with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the head of this intestinal thread, which is much stripped, and then tie it to the head of this thin flaxen thread twisted, then wind the thread into the needle, and stitch the intestine, and rearrange it in the rupture; and this method of stitching foreign bodies is not stronger than according to reason and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, no one can heal it with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, whether it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Every wound or abscess, when it becomes infected, is generally called a "fistula", especially when it is covered with pus and feels warm.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is according to the true nodation, hard and white, where no pain is felt, and is just as covered with pus as the feathers of a bird; and it never clears up clearly, sometimes being thin and other times thick; sometimes moist, and other times dry; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not clean, and has no discharge, is solely due to one of nine causes: namely, too much blood or pus; or because of its evil nature; or because there is hard matter inside, preventing it from discharging; or because there is excessive moisture; or because the flesh is rotten and the material of poor quality; or if the medicine is not good for healing; or because the corruption has the manner of a plague; or because the property of the region causes late digestion, slow health, and flatulence by nature; or it has veins or bones. And I have already explained all these causes, their signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, and nerves, or the small intestine, bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine in the back, or any joints of the hands or feet, and they can also affect the primary member and its associated parts.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is no cure but labor and ignorance; if there is a fistula that does not come to the place I mentioned above, and you have confidence in the treatment and understand it, take a piece of steel or iron, if the fistula is straight, cut it as desired; and if it is crooked, seek a delicate tool for plugging, because the plug bends itself around the curvature. Then wash it thoroughly with water to remove moisture and impurities; afterward, cut it precisely at your ability, that you may know if there are bones or nerves, and if it is completely healed, and ask the patient in pain where they feel it when you press your hand, and the location where they feel it; once you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or any of the places I mentioned, then cut it as I told you, and remove all the harmful tissue and corrupted flesh inside; and then treat it as long as it is clean, and if the fistula is deep and straight, cut it completely, as much as you can, then apply moistened medical herbs over it, and cover it with a bottle up to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; then apply clean, healthy bandages, as long as it heals; and if it does not heal by this method, cauterize it as we said before, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the principal member, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, treat it until the corruption is completely removed, then apply curative remedies so long as it remains sound; but if it is not sound and bends back as before, know that you are not yet safe. Expose it and keep it until you reach the depths, and remove all the corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it is thus sound, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If no, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot cure it; if there is no other cause than to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can extract with pincers, using an appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, break them not, but remove every bit of them; and if moisture makes things worse and there is doubt or fear, dry it and bind it up, and heat and massage the bone.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, apply something corruptible to the wound, and let it fester until the bones are rotten within, and then they will be more easily removed; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, scrape away the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then close the wound; and if there is a great part corrupted, extending almost to the bone, you must cover it completely until the corruption is healed, and then treat it until it is sound; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example from it and use aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old who had a pain in his leg due to something that came from within the body, causing matters to accumulate in the leg, and he was afflicted with a large abscess, for which there was no reason to open; but through their folly, they worked so much on the abscess that it opened, and many substances corroded, becoming a fistula, and numerous ruptures that caused bowing and moisture from the body. Many tried to cure him for two years, and none of them were skilled in manual arts, until I was called to see his leg and the medications they used, and what was wrong through the ruptures affecting the whole body; and the young man's skin turned red, with a citrine-like hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then I examined all the openings, and found that some came against each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then quickly entered one of the openings and cut as deep as I discovered a piece of bone, which was corrupted and perforated, and the corruption extended to the bone itself; I understood what appeared to be the corrupt bone, and thought that there was no other corruption besides that which I left; and I began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, but they could not heal it; then I re-examined it and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, so I treated it and then closed it, and focused on binding the place; but I could not do so until I had removed a palm-sized piece of the bone, and brought it back to its original shape. Then I treated it with medicines again, and it healed steadily and was bound securely, and did not want to start over again except for the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the evacuation of blood, it often happens completely, and a hard callus is formed in its place on the bone, which is well arranged and causes no harm or damage to anything at all, neither coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a ligature, and stretch it over the end of the bone that opens, and instruct anyone to pull it upwards; and attach another thicker woolen ligature to the first one, and bind it over the char (fragment) where the bone is, so that you pull the char from below, and uncover the char on the bone where you observe it to be, so that the bone does not become infected with the charred part; and place a small piece of charcoal or a table under the bone to cover the infected char; and it should be treated as much as possible to be seen and felt, and then in this way once more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover the entire limb; then apply heat from below, and then move the affected part to the other side of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupt joint, and remove the bone from the other side; and if the corruption is in the connection between two joints, there is no other way but to cut it off; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or at the ankle of the foot, this matter is very difficult, but nevertheless you must inquire about this corruption how it opens, and cleanse it in every way that you can, as long as the vein or nerve do not oppose; and know that there are many instruments for cutting and binding these bones, according to the position of the bone and its appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason, it is necessary to match each instrument with the shape of each wound; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; therefore choose the instrument that is right for the job.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint becomes dislocated either internally or externally; and when you have treated that corruption with medicinal remedies but they do not help, then it is necessary to cover that limb until the corruption reaches the joint where it originates, so that the patient escapes from death or evil, which is greater, due to the fault in the limb; and the signs of this are that the limb turns black, seeming to be burned by fire, and after the blackening, because these corrosions spread from one limb to another and take over the whole body; therefore, hurry to cover it, and if it is caused by the bite of some poisonous creature, such as a sea scorpion or serpent or similar, then if the corruption is at the top of the two joints, treat it immediately and do not allow any space for it to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, it should cup the joint so that corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes up to the arm, it should cup the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no cure outside of its quantity of virtue; and thus it acts when corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, it cups after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, it cups the entire foot; and if it goes up the leg, it cups at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cupping or binding the member is that you tie it above and below, and stretch one assistant with the lower string, and another assistant with the upper string, and you remove the skin that is between the two strings with a wide spatula, until the bone is exposed; then cup or bind, and place a strip of linen on each side so that the linen does not touch the healthy part, and it brings the patient further injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the discharge of pus occurs when you open it, and you cauterize the wound too aggressively, or apply any restraining powders; then return to your medicine as soon as it is complete, tie the afflicted limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you that it happened to a man in great pain: he had a blackening which seemed to be a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his right foot, discoloring it entirely; and when he saw the corrosion, he covered his foot, and it healed; but long after, the corrosion returned on his left hand, and he came to me, and I applied reflective things after purification of the body, and the corrosion would not cease. And he begged me to amputate his hand, but I did not want to do so, as I had hope of reflecting the material. And I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, since the strength of the man was weak; and he became completely desperate, returned to his land, covered his hand, and it healed; and I have only heard this tale told about anyone else who does otherwise, when necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess ever forms in a fleshy joint, and it stays there so long that it causes great tension; then it ruptures and pierces the flesh, leaving the bones visible, just like a vessel; and the skin covering it is as thin as delicate cloth, and does not extend to the bone or nerve, and such an illness is called 'sain' (healthy), and not 'fistule' (abscess); but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, it is called a 'fistule'; and the skin should be cut all around, especially when it is thin like cloth; and its corruption is not known.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you believe the skin is infected and the corruption is not completely healed, and the skin is dry and hard, treat it with a cleansing enema as follows: examine if the breast is swollen and emits a foul odor; then administer an Egyptian medicine made of equal parts of salt, oil, litargire (a type of mercury), and heat them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thick like honey. Then, according to need, dilute it with water and honey and apply it to the affected area, constricting the aperture; leave the medicine for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; repeat this several times until the breast is cleansed and any pus is drained. If the infected person cannot tolerate either the Egyptian medicine or hot water, use a mixture of hot water and ground charcoal from vine wood, pour it over the affected area, let it flow, and apply the enema; continue this until you are certain the breast is thoroughly cleansed. Alternatively, use an enema made with honey and fermented wine, allowing the honey to purify and wash away the infection, while the wine promotes healing. If the aperture of the breast is too small for the enema tube, enlarge it slightly with a hot iron, then apply a thin layer of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is wide enough for the enema to pass through. If the wound is excessively large and cannot be sufficiently widened for the enema, and the discharge from the affected area flows downwards, ensure that the enema tube is positioned higher than the infected site.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, it does not allow gas to form; and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves down to its lowest point, for when the bowel is perfect, it does not allow gas to form, and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you see fit, arrange it so the bowel moves slightly downwards, and leave nothing of the bowels; take consolidative medicines to place over the wound, and put a linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then, stitch as strongly around the perforation in the side of the anus, making it wider than before, for often, to remove the bowels, they remove the anus; and know what runs from the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or enough or digested or undigested; be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or no, and when you see how your medicine has spread in such a way over the perforation in the side of the anus, then know that the bowels are already healing, and bring back health; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast feels bowed and indigest after many days, knowing that it will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons manifest after a long time, do not despair of your health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are some whose symptoms worsen when they speak about their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if the breast feels bowed and closed after many days, knowing that it will not open; and if the breast is slow to open and remains shut, then use moist medicines with a subtle effect, as an ointment prepared with vitriol, which is the last medicine; take this delicate ointment and mix it with rose oil, adding equal parts of good wine; then conserve it and apply it. The same method can be used for making honey thickened with cooked grain, when a delicate ointment is not available; you may take mirra, aloes, and incense, crush them, and sprinkle the powder over honey while it is still warm; then spread it on a cloth and place it on the breast; never apply it directly or use roots of lotus, which is similar to flour or chalk; and use simple or composite remedies: grind them into a powder and mix them with the honey I mentioned, and apply it. If the cure prolongs, and this treatment does not help, then know that corruption has taken hold, and it exerts pressure on bones, limbs, or joints; just as we said earlier about treating fistulas.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is an abscess that arises from the nail, either in the hand or the foot, or occasionally elsewhere; and when it becomes old and one does not take care, it leads to a gangrenous infection, causing pain and swelling until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly even destroys the entire nail. It results in putrid odor, the affected area becomes red and swollen, and the limb feels cold.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When treating it as we have described in the previous section, if the treatment is not effective, then you must remove all the dead tissue from around the nail, and after that, cauterize the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound; if the nail pierces the flesh, and begins to poke, and the wound bleeds, it is necessary that you place the right edge under the nail where it pricks, and pull it up high, and gently and softly sever that flesh, and apply hot and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat the wound with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it, and dig out the rot, for as much as the bone decays, it cannot heal; and if you see both bones decaying, remove them immediately as mentioned above, then treat it until it heals; and if it is frozen, and swollen, and causes great pain, it is necessary that you treat it first; then cut the nail with a sharp spatumile across from above, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain so sharp and intense strikes the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	He who is born into the hands of no one, perhaps quite fleshy, and by chance has a part with bones, but never a nail, and none are born in the root of the joint, where birth is against nature.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in no joint shall not move, and he who is born in the joint of a joint may be immobile; the size of the fleshy one is so slight, in such a manner: cut him at his root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the jointure is difficult to cure; if it keeps you awake.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born with or develop a deformity, it is necessary that you first hold the round shape of the joint firmly towards the bone, then dislocate the bone to a suitable position, and finally cure it as long as it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come together in a joint may be due to birth, or the healing of a wound, or burns from fire, or similar conditions.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you need to secure that joint, so it must be repaired according to their natural forms; then place between two moistened linen or cloth in rose oil, so they do not adhere; or you place between two pieces of fine leather, as long as the limbs are joined, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs in any of its fingers with the palm, secure that joint as appropriate.
des vils	venoms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	These veins are thickly wrapped, filled with excessive melancholic substances that affect various members of the body; and they occur more frequently in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry heavy loads, compared to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary for you to administer purgative once and then cleanse the bowels.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of fire is according to two manners: one is with the use of cups and extraction of black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and drain it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The operation is performed in this manner: first, immerse the leg in hot water as much as possible without causing pain, then extract the affected limb from the knee to the ankle; then cut the vein in one or two or three places with a large incision, drain and squeeze out the black blood into your hand from one end to the other, until such time as the patient can bear it; then bind it, and order him to eat food causing black vomit; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harm the patient not.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	They should raise the affected leg, if there are many hairs, then immerse it in hot water, and raise it with warm water until the veins turn red and swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over fire, and then compress it against the vein close to the knee, or on the inside of the ankle. Then open the skin near the vein, scraping it from both sides until it is exposed, and you see it red and black, resembling a white cord; then pull from below until it is lifted from the skin, and then gently press it at the other end, as you did before; then cut another piece, if necessary, and lift it, and compress it against the vein again, moving to another hook, as you did previously; then cut another piece, and lift it, and compress and cut the vein at the second hook, until it is completely extracted, then clean it. And if you cannot extract it, insert a very strong needle through the entire thread, bind and pull it, and pull from below, turning your hand back and forth, until it comes out; beware that it does not cut off, for if it does, you will not be able to extract or lift it, and harm will come to the patient. And once extracted, place a moist, soft cloth over the wound, steeped in wine and rose oil, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the limb is contracted and twisted and bent together, not in a straight position as we have said, then it must be torn apart forcibly, but not covered; treat it as we have mentioned above.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape to use when closing the eye is very curved, and it does not cut through, only closing the eyelid; it is of great curvature, because if it were thin, it would cut the eyelid, but since it must be thick as we have said, this is its form.
de la voinne civile	of the natural vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in warm regions where no plants or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that arises from beneath the skin, as it comes from within the body coiled and twisted.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to emerge forcefully, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two finger widths, leaving the cloth on the leg, and whenever it retracts, re-wrap around the cloth, and do not cover its root until it has completely emerged; for if you cut it, it will recede into the flesh, causing abscesses, putrefaction, or other illness. Therefore, it is important to treat it little by little until it is fully healed, leaving no cloth in the body; and this vein appears when it is treated with five or ten long finger-widths of cloth, as has come to me personally, where it emerged from ten finger-widths long, and when you cut it, it draws back one or two holes, and pierces to the bottom so that all can see; and it should be emptied of the matter inside, and treated with medicines that prevent putrefaction for several days, then cure it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never again touch this vein, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or of the hand, and a great deal of blood flows out; from which it often jumps and spouts; treat it then as we have said above.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between skin and bone.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "bull disease" in our land because it often affects bulls, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and bone.
