It spreads throughout the body, moving from one member to another, causing great pain as it bursts through the skin where it resides, and sometimes it goes into the eye, perhaps entering and damaging it; this happens repeatedly. It is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, just like worms, serpents, or lice in the belly, and its malice is uncertain, for when it moves through the body and reaches the head, it can affect the eye, and if it enters, it may destroy it. This occurs frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and draining, it cannot be done unless the pus has formed: therefore, it is necessary that you hold the limb above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut and drain it thoroughly, and if the pus is thick in the wound, cauterize it with fire until it dries up; and the greater harm it causes, the more it will discharge oil, as we have said; and if you see the swelling coming near the oil gland, stretch it below the eyebrow, then cut and drain it thoroughly; and it is advisable for the patient to use purification of the body with solvents and medicines to dispel bad humors, and to avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but moves from one member to another; and I have seen this as I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and after that, I saw something rise up on her shoulder, as quickly as anything, like bright silver when it cuts through flesh; the pain left that place and moved to the shoulder, and then, a little later, spread throughout her body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she felt it move around inside her body, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how it moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had observed that everyone wanted to move the pain from one place to another, but I hadn't seen it like this before, as I did with the woman; and I thought it was because she had a dry body, her veins exposed, and this constricted movement; and I didn't see it apply to those who are delighted, with moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease heal, and the patient feels that pain as we have said, if it opens from top to bottom and then closes until that constricted movement in the place subsides; and cauterize the place; and if you do not have these remedies, cure it with those who dispel stiffness, such as foul pills, serpentary pills, and similar ones.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows vary, according to their appearance and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity lies in that they have large and small tips, some are smooth, others are sealed; and there are those with two points, and those with lengths, and some with pieces; and some pierce any member in two ways: either in a primary member, such as the head, body, liver, kidney, intestines, bladder, or similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes out in any part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: it is necessary that you fight for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various ways; and if this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully extracted, remove it, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow comes out and pierces the bone, and if there is satisfaction in the area above the brain, it is when the sight, side vision, and eye movements are impaired and red, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and clouding of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without feeling from the nostrils or ears; and possibly losing speech and voice; and also coming out as white pus-like fluid from the wound, and sometimes like a burning sensation in the chest; and if these signs appear to you, since you are in charge of the cure, remove the arrow even if it is not completely embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of an arrow when it breaks or withdraws, is that it is close to the left breast and feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not empty; and sometimes the arrow remains silent like a pulse, and brings black blood, cold and sweating, and fainting: know therefore without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that the patient never sweats is that no foam comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns pale, and he breathes heavily and stops moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow comes out in the night, it leaves small holes; and causes great pain and sorrow and heavy breathing; and all the muscles of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces through the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces through the belly, and there is no sign of healing through the intestines, then there is little hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and the urine jumps out and overflows, and the patient feels intense pain, know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, as they are formed and their joints and neck and shoulder and helper (muscles) and the sharp pain in the back and the forceful and stiffening (of muscles), and the foot and legs, and the appearance of the limb, differ according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you must do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There once happened to me at home an arrow that penetrated my eye or cheek: I tried to pull it out, and pushed it from the other side through the fat of the ear, and it was healed without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And at another time, he pulled out an arrow that had penetrated the fat under the skin without damaging the papilla, and the arrow was completely extracted, leaving only the tip in the flesh, and it was a large arrow with a blue arc, surprisingly light without any damage to the ear; he was healed, and no further harm came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And extract an arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was an arrow with ears [perhaps referring to barbs or a specific type of arrowhead]: I trimmed the barb and drew it out gently, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow that was stuck in a man's home, which had penetrated his gut, and I thought he was dying; but after thirty days, he showed no change in condition; so I cut around the arrow, and freed it, and pulled it out without any ill effect.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help a man who has an arrow stuck in his back or chest, and the wound is deep; and the arrow remains trapped within him, and he shows no change in his natural condition, nor does he experience any harm from any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man to whom an arrow struck his face and deeply wounded him; he endured much without suffering great pain; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated a prince, the king himself, who had an arrow in his neck that was deeply embedded and slightly tilted to the right side; the arrow was completely lodged, and I was called to treat it after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I carefully probed it, and I felt nothing; however, he experienced sharp pain and discomfort underneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I placed a soothing, digestive plaster on the shoulder because the muscles were not tightening; and then I saw the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the plaster on for several days, then healed the wound and thus the patient endured great pain for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his neck; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it opened and I felt the tip of the arrow sticking in the flesh; then I adjusted the opening of the wound with that medicine until the head of the arrow became visible; and it healed after about three months, but then the wound opened up again, so I used tweezers to pull on both sides without success. Then I did not stop trying to find subtle and ingenious tools, until I finally got hold of well-made tweezers, as described at the end of this chapter, and I pulled it out and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they consider that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: so I restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have also told you about the quality of removing certain arrows, so that you place your care on what I do not say, for books cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare well enough small things and those present and deficient, true new works and new instruments, for the descent of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the members where they are embedded, except in two ways: either through the vein where they enter, or from another part; and that which comes out from the side where it enters is an arrow embedded in the flesh, and it never comes out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it stay until the flesh around it becomes rotten and open; and if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and each day move it a little; and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce through everything with a thin knife until the bones around it are widened.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the top and goes all the way to one of the belly cavities near the brain, and none of the things I have mentioned earlier help the patient: do not pull it out, but let it stay even for several days, for if it comes close to the center, it will be fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not come out satisfactorily, it leaves the patient no rest for days without further harm, if the skill of pulling it out is lacking.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply heat around it, as I have told you; then cure the joint while it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is withdrawn into the flesh of the body and cannot be seen, one should attempt to pull it with all strength; and if you feel it, use any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, or there are no bones, muscles, or nerves nearby, leave it until the wound is severe; and if possible, pull the arrow, and if there are any pieces of bone attached on either side that you can remove, dislocate the arrowhead from its position as much as you can, then break or bend the arrow's tail, so you can pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, so that the limb is entirely relaxed around the joint, then continue to treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the signs of blood poisoning appear to you, then follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter; and be careful with the incision on the nerve and the vein, and find a way to extract the arrow without danger, as soon or as late, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position it was in when the arrow left, for that is the greatest help, and if you cannot, then do what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	He knows the arrow that comes from another place, where it opens something within, and the skin is swollen in that area as one can see or feel apparently: then cut there, until the pliers can grasp it, and then extract it: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be extracted, leave it for now, and then try to extract it again until it comes out; and if there is an arrowhead in the bone, it should be pushed into the center of the instrument, and then forced out, and if the arrow is removed with the instrument, the extraction will be easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you clean all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow has pierced through to the abdomen or bladder or ribcage, and it is close to the surface, and you can reach it, then take care to remove it; avoid cutting into the vein or nerve, then extract the arrow, and clean the wound as best you can, and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The instrument used to extract arrows resembles a bird's beak; here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like a feather, to point the tip of the arrow, just as if it were the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pincers, to pierce and hold if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can gain health, of which there are 16 main ones: 2 battan veins behind the ears, called "herbech"; and 2 arteries appearing in the two temples, and 2 veins in the two arm pits, called "aspires"; and the vein across the forehead; and the vein at the top of the head near the nose; and the 2 glands at the collarbone; and 2 veins in the upper lip above the mouth, called "augeherich"; and 2 veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly draws health are 5 in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side, and common people call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins; and common people call it "vein of the body" and is on the right side. The basilic is situated at the bottom, and common people call it "vein of the belly", and it lies above the femoral vein, and that's the one from which health is drawn, which opens clearly onto the palm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saving vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one below the knee on the left side, and the second is the thin one at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called 'nesse' is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins behind the ears aid in the discharge of old catarrh and migraine; and the quality of the vein, as I have said, is that you raise the patient's head and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then squeeze the patient's collar tightly until the two veins beneath the ears extend in two parts from the head: hold them there, and wherever you feel the pulse beneath your hand, it signifies improvement; then take the lance and bore through the vein just below the bone, and lift your hand up the entire vein upstream, and cut and the skin and flesh and the vein well away from the bone, and let out the blood until you see; then strain and bind it, as long as it remains healthy; and I have already spoken of incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, as it were, an old and smooth process, and accustomed to sight, and the body of sharp tears with them; and the quality of healing is such as I say: and it is that the patient pulls his collar tight, as long as the two veins remain open; he feels the pulse under his finger, then signs with a cross; then lightly presses on the vein higher down on his little finger, and withdraws the needle from under, and releases the vein higher up, and the clot, just as you did with the other veins, and makes the blood flow according to your need; then unties the patient, and puts his finger on the vein for an hour, then puts cotton; then forms a bandage and leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken much of their cleansing and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The surgeon of the vein on the forehead is just as valuable as the surgeon of the skull for ancient face diseases and migraine and redness; and its quality is such that the patient tightens his neck by twisting, until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "borer", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another tool, allowing the blood to flow according to the amount you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy without opening a wide wound.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too strong; and do not cut across the healthy flesh, for the bone is close by, and by chance might break the flame when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins located in the arms is beneficial for wounds, itching, redness, and eye conditions, as well as facial diseases; its quality lies in that the patient's condition does not worsen due to any strain or twisting of the veins, as would happen otherwise. Then, regarding the vein, it should be neither too thin nor too thick with fire, for there is no middle ground.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the fire is subtle, it may burn; then draw out the blood slowly, as much as needed, and then bind it with cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein near the nose is very valuable for colds, sudden fever, and facial ailments such as migraines and redness that appear on the face, especially when it is old. The quality of this health is that the patient tightens his neck and pulls his nose to his left hand; he then inserts a subtle long flame into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well enough for the blood to flow, and the healing begins now. Do not dig too deep, and draw out the blood slowly according to your need, then bandage it for a night, as it is quickly restored; this is the shape of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The holy oil of the two guindges is helpful for the narrowing of the eye, and the onset of illness, and many diseases, and fever, and corrosion, and herpes, and boils; and its quality is such that it extracts the patient's pain from both sides, as we have said; and the skilled one who treats the patient's head, and the patient lies on a seat, then cleans the vein with long and slightly wide strokes, then applies blood-letting in a temperate manner, or as needed; then repeat this process in the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and gently tighten the veins so that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until morning, for the wound to heal.
de la sainie des leivres	from the health of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins in the mouth helps to prevent colds, and the corruption of gums, splits in the lips, and pain and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to have the patient sit in front of you, holding his chin as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which you recognize by their black color and small veins around them: so cut both, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, cut the thicker one from each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the cleansing of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The cleansing of the tongue is most beneficial after the cleansing of the head, and it helps with conditions in the throat, and eye diseases, and mouth ailments; and the quality of the cleansing is such that the patient should hold the tongue between their hands towards the sun, and gently pull it, examining each side for a black vein: cleanse both, but do not force too hard, as they are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins in the neck that are commonly cleansed are done in two ways: either by pressing with a hot flame immediately, or using a delicate knife, like a scalpel, and this is called "aneisling"; and they are large and small according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the fevered area turns red and is very renowned, and it is large as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins with smooth and flat openings full of obvious thick blood, which contain thick blood and mucus; and this is the shape of the olive-colored fever.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicately pointed, and is for healing the delicate veins where there is subtle citrus-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is very helpful for diseases that are below the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the belly; and it is important for the healer to heal gently and wash out the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the artery, and blood flow stops, as is necessary, as I said; and the flame should not be gripping, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and change it for another; or you want none of its blood, and heal the wound to the vein in the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it with a knife, as we said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you come to know the place of the wound, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touch the wound until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with a sign, and bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife, as we said; and be careful not to harm the artery when you see it swell, for that is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bubbling up from above like a child's urine, and the eyes are red and thin, know that it is a sign of an artery: so hurry, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding has stopped, which often happens; if the arm is bound, leave it alone, and do not move the patient until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the eye is not stained and it bleeds, and no remedy comes to mind, if the artery opens up, especially near its root; stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fig bark, cut it, and take one half and bind it firmly to the other side; if it stays in place, that's good. If not, treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood flow; binding is not too tight or loose for the size of the wound, and it should be done with skill.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	If the vein is infected, help by treating the blood flow from the top and the bottom, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; the healer should wash for the nerve below, and if it is not too deep, and he finds the nerve, it swells and the healing is hindered, and perhaps it cannot heal; this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person due to its subtlety, then it must be treated with an antiseptic instrument beforehand, and be careful with the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if a vein is between the two bones, it makes it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment for the headache is to draw blood from the forehead, which helps the limbs; and it is beneficial to apply olive or myrtle flame, as it is the safest of all veins, as it does not affect any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is advisable to seek the lightest vein, and do not be concerned if it hurts the first time, just try again; and sometimes the veins swell up in some men when they are punctured for the first time, but it should not hurt.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound healing depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that healing is not only achieved by maintaining health and preventing future ailments; it involves one of the three main veins: cephalics, femoral, or basilic. One should begin healing in the early stages of illness, during autumn and winter after eating, when signs of satiety appear. One should heal on the first day or third day, after 2-3 hours or the second day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Healing that is administered for ailments does not have a fixed time, but rather when there is a need for it, at any hour and in all seasons; however, one should not heal children until they are 12-13 years old, nor pregnant women after just four weeks until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not treat the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be healed in any way, it is necessary for him to cleanse the intestines with a light enema if he has a lot of feces retained, so that the veins do not draw out the harmful excesses from the primary members; nor should one heal someone who is too salt from meat, or raw, as long as they are thus, nor those who are waterlogged, after colic, vomiting, belly pain, frequent defecation, much sexual activity, hard work, watching, fasting, and this, whether due to a weapon or bodily weakness; then carefully remove the humors, if they are thick, through food and drinks and medicines, if you have cause to do so; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, in order to purify the blood, and heal the vein from below towards the third, as we have said; and guard yourself on that day against work, fatigue, luxury, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and let the healing be more thorough than that of others; then rub the arm twice or three times, then tighten the ligature slightly, for when it is too tight, it cannot heal; and then rub it with your hands until the veins swell up and you feel them. Then moisten the compress with a little old oil, then place your left hand's finger on the vein under the skin slightly where you want to heal, so that the vein does not burst or injure itself.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as if tied to the body, and if they are of such a kind that they are afflicted with pus, so that when fire is applied, it draws back from the fire, and cannot open the vein, then one suffers from this; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the surgeon must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, it is good; but if not, one must try again a little further from the previous point, if the limb is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is inflamed and the patient fears, let it be for one or two days without binding it; perhaps it will form an abscess later. Do not put him in a bath, but continue treatment as it pleases the surgeon; and if the perforation is small, pierce it subtly and gently so as not to draw out too much blood, as you see fit; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein engorged, do not immediately recommence bleeding, but apply a little oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and the oil moves in this vein the substance that the oil itself; and thus administer the oil in each wound that you treat veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same is done trially and gently when it is applied to the shoulder; it thins the blood and disperses it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess occurs, which happens frequently, especially when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and apply a moist sponge with hot water and silk, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood flow from the vein has stopped, and if it stays in place for several days without turning black or green, it will not harm; and if you see, apply any aloe or myrrh prepared in calament juice, a poultice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling appear in the holy basil: then place your hand above, and if you feel the soft joint under the pressure of your hand, it is this appearance that is harmful.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be careful not to place anything on it that we have mentioned, for it may dry out and become hard without the flow of blood; but make an ointment to harden the joint, then apply other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each case of pain according to the quantity of its strength and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the wound is infected, let it drain as long as it remains red; and if you see a large amount of pus, let it continue to drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is strong and robust, and has the skill to extract pus, to make a larger wound, with wider flaps; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, making smaller and more frequent wounds, and always cutting across, not piercing. This method of dressing saves from infection and damage to nerves, and is better than long and wide dressings.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body requires cleansing, it is necessary to apply a mild mixture of pomegranate juice; if he is overheated, he should take bloodletting three or four times. And if he has a cold constitution, he should eat before cleansing a mild mixture of syrup, either mused syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chives, and a very fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during cleansing, after the release of much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a brew of charcoal and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope for vein evacuation.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to straighten his arm and heal it later, if it is weakened by much blood loss, he should pull it little by little, according to the amount of its strength continues.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to straighten his arm after the first dressing and has a strong contraction, he should heal it seven hours after the first dressing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another side, he should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body, which has already been heated, and causes fever; it needs to be drained in large quantities, and the opening widened until it takes possession of the entire limb; then you must apply all the conditions of health, and place your hand upon its pulse when it's healing, so that death does not come in the absence of warmth, which happens often when healthcare is neglected; and you should never, when freeing the arm, cause blood to flow out again or reopen the wound, but press firmly upon it; nor if it's twisted, should you force it straight, for that would be harmful; but let it heal fully a second time; or if there's a point at the tip of the flame, until the blood which is congealed within the vein leaves and puts itself back into water, and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflated, leave it alone and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to drain blood a second time due to the abscess recurring in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein from the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method for healing is that the patient should hold his hand in hot water until the veins are red, then tie it slightly so that the vein appears well, and then heal it from now on across, not too wide or too long; and make the punctures wide, and heal close to the joint of the hand, without letting any blood escape, and return the hand to hot water and let the blood flow in the water until you have enough; and if it is in this state, do not stop holding the hand in hot water because it is put into greater heat than necessary; and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The surgeon of salvation of the right hand is worthy of all diseases that affect the flesh; and this is the manner: stretch out the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein is engorged, if you see it; and if the wound is diagonal, and if you touch it with your whole hand, nothing should hurt; but do not press too hard, for the nerve is entirely devoid of flesh, and then dip the hand back into hot water, if it feels numb in the wound, and it cannot issue forth.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, then apply oil and string to seal the wound tightly, and do so for every person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person holds the eye with their left hand to cure the disease of the mouse, and does everything as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The healer of the soul holds itself to all diseases that afflict the body, such as illnesses of the heart, and retention of flowers (possibly referring to a condition related to flora or a metaphorical 'blooming' issue), and diseases of rain (potentially meteor-related or a metaphor for humidity-linked ailments), and old joints and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his health is such that patients experience great relief in hot water, rubbing their veins until they subside, and binding them over the joints of the foot. The vein is located at the ankle, and above the foot, it goes up to the knee; this method is therefore useful for either a heavy downpour (of fluid) or at the ankle, wherever it is most needed.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bind it on the foot, be careful not to constrict the toes, and apply the bandage as if you were tying a knot; and the pain will subside.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the pain cannot be relieved, immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to drain completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the bandaging is done for the first time, repeat the process slightly above the previous one, as the toes are stiff; do not doubt and constrict the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the foot's ankle, and its health corresponds to the pain of the back when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its health is such that the patient feels better in the bath, straining from the ankle with three or four stretches, otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, the health in all ways as you can, and crossing; and should be moved as you cover it, for the lion is safe, and it is greatly relieved by manual manipulation.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not succeed, there is no flow of health from the vein that opens on the back or side of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nails; and make sure with blood as much as possible, and then loosen the bandage, and put cotton on it and tighten it; it is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	from the suction of the cupping glass
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and the suction is created in two ways: either by striking and attracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This suction, performed without striking, is carried out in two ways: either entirely with heat or without heat; and the suction, when blood is struck and extracted, is done in twelve parts of the body, one over the forehead, another across the nape of the neck, two on each shoulder, one under the chin, two on each arm, and two on each leg, also two on each ankle. The suction does not involve drawing blood from veins but rather from small vessels scattered throughout the skin; it does not weaken anyone as is done with vein-cutting treatments, and it should never be carried out on a patient suffering from congestion due to recent overeating, while the body is still full.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness or habits it needs to be ventosed, in the beginning and at the end of each month, and every day, for there are such who when they need to be ventosed, their head becomes heavy; and others who experience swelling and redness on their face, and their head, and neck, and darkness; and such who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue is swollen, and they bleed; and others who think, see blackness, nausea, and die, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order it to be ventosed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The surgeon of the muscle is aided by the heat in the great pain ... that comes from the dislocation, and it does not suit that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this application is for the health of the head, and it does not suit those of cold complexion who use it, or who have scabs, because they cause them much harm; and for this reason the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold headaches.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become obstructed, and for this reason a suction cup should be placed slightly lower in doubt of obstruction.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the chest is beneficial for the health of the heart and lungs, and because of this, it causes tightness in the chest, constriction of the channel of the lung, and sometimes, swelling and bloating; and it should be relieved quickly, because if it holds too firmly, it can cause harm to the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation of the chest as it affects the ribs can cause headaches, eye pain, constriction, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is beneficial for the health of the heart and lungs; therefore, you should instruct the patient to gently press their hand against the chest, avoiding pressure on the artery, to prevent bleeding or other complications.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The inflammation of the gums is valuable in mouth diseases, and in the decay of teeth, and similar ailments in the mouth, and it affects the health of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammation of the shoulders is associated with disease that arises from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The inflammation of the veins is as significant as three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to press too hard, for the skin over the veins is bare, and it can damage the veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the croup is as harmful as bruises from the bottom, and it causes diseases below, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and made of iron, so that it needs to be carefully pulled; and if it is too delicate, it will break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs close tightly as they draw blood from all over the body and cause severe pain in the old rains, and joints, and bladder, and result in scars; they are located on the two knees and two ankles, but they weaken the body after long use and lead to more stiffness.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a suction cup is as follows: you apply it at first while it is empty, and suck gently, then place it firmly and move it evenly without stopping until you see the skin turn red and swollen, and open the veins; then remove them, and be careful with the position of the cups, for there are some with thick skin and narrow pores: it is only necessary to apply them once, making large wounds and deep ones slightly; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: first to open the way for the thick vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very sharp, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we suffice with only one blow.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we must often strike; and if the pain is sharp, let us make sure to pierce the end suddenly; it is suitable for those who have thick and hard skin, and who are covered with hair, to apply oil from suction cups that both opens and closes: this can be violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in ivy, watercress oil, or lilies, or chamomile, or another similar plant.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balm of Gilead, or donkey oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if anyone has a skin that is too sensitive and has narrow pores, it is not advisable to apply oil, but instead, after cleansing with rosewater, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of calabash, or water of porcelain, or any similar thing, they should wash it.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with excessive moisture, they should rise from it using myrrh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive superfluities should rise from old wine, or sage water, or nettles or chamomile decoction, or other similar things; and it is not suitable to use a cupping glass before a bath or after a bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he washes himself when he needs to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware that the one who is healthy has a temperamental constitution and if he is too hot and inflamed; it is necessary for him to press cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuces in moderation, and similar things; and eat little, and light meals of chickpeas, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should sip syrup of honey and medium scented wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat few seeds and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he takes fresh air, he must drink more than he eats; and it is fitting to give any man at any time triacle or nutmeg before or after ventilation, to strengthen the principal members; but he who is hot should not drink it.
