Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and the spleen, and podagra, and the belly and the bowels and the kidneys and the hip joint, for these members do not tolerate injury at once, and they are only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we place suction cups on the mammary glands when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put suction cups on the belly and bowels to reduce the member's size; and it removes pain when there is congestion or a stone, so it may possibly draw the congestion away, or leave the stone from its place; and thus does it act when placed on the liver and spleen where there is retained wind, and these suction cups are left empty to suck only; and they are never at once very hot, nor filled with cold water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in such a way we fill the cup with hot water mixed with suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should have a width of two and a half palm lengths, and on one side, near the center, it should have a small hole, as wide as to fit an needle, and be made of iron or steel, so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in its middle, there should be a crossbar also of iron or steel, to hold a cloth for suction, and their sizes vary according to the illness and age of those who use them, for the suction cups for children are different from those for adults, and for thin people compared to fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one should place this suction cup over the member: take the wax cloth or linen, and place it through the hole in the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup, preventing it from burning the patient; then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the opening we have mentioned, so that when you wish, the vapor goes out, and you remove the suction cup; and use the linen as before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is applied to treat pleurisy, or any acute condition, there should be no hole or opening, and it is only effective when completely filled with water, then placed on the member; its shape is as follows:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without wounds that are so small that they cannot be bound with cupping glasses, such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and in places where the skin is stripped of hair, like a doe or a hare, and other similar areas; and if the quality of the wound is such that when you touch the wounds that are in clean, sweet water without putrefaction, they take it; and place them in clean, sweet water until they become familiar and have nothing in their stomachs; then clean with a vein and cupping glass, rub the limb until it turns red, and apply the cups; and when they are painful and scream, if it is a part where a cup can be applied, apply it, for this helps greatly afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If the lion does not leave its den, take a large quantity of water and mix it with some good earth, then expect (the lion's recovery); and if the lion's wounds are too deep after the operation, moisten a linen cloth with cold water, place it on top, until the wounds are healed; and if the wounds multiply, put vitriol or gall or similar substances, until they are healed; or you can put half-peeled fava beans on the wound and leave them until they adhere to the lion; then it will heal. If more is needed, take other lions.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the lions refuse to be taken, rub fresh lion's blood on them or insert an arrow into their wound until they bleed, then place them back; and soon as they smell the blood, they will adhere (to each other); and when you see that they are chewing, sprinkle a little aloe and silk powder or ash, and they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear reader, that the folly of the eyes often deceives one from this chapter, for they have never seen or read it in any ancient book; and because of this, the knowledge is strange to our land, for I have found no good books on it, save through the study of ancient texts, over which I have labored much, and by experience, and from the habits of my life. And so I have described to you, in this chapter, what it contains, and abridged it at the end, and made clear the shapes of the instruments that are employed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we explain in this prologue of this book the essence of the words and the chapters where the wise apply their understanding, focusing on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation or twist occurs, it is necessary that you promptly tend to the patient on both sides, if nothing helps, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age; or if he has a fever, or too much cold, and consumes cold things like ice, and does not eat any fatty food, and does not overfill himself with meat that fills the veins, until you have no doubt of an abscess or spreading of material in the limb; then the patient returns to his former state as if nothing had happened.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be relieved of the foods that cause heavy digestion, or have a viscous quality, like cooked flour in water, and rice, and vegetables, and wine, and fresh fish, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For heavy digestion often returns and makes the injury worse.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of old people and decrepit individuals cannot heal or fuse well according to their nature due to the stiffness of the members, nor can those that are too soft, like the bones of young children; but take no notice, hold onto the broken bone with strong grips that unite the member together, as it was before, and do not restrict its movement completely, and for this reason, relieve them of heavy foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and in this chapter, I will tell you all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, just like the edge of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if the fracture is with a wound, and there is a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each condition has its own mechanism and specific tool for restoration, according to the memory that comes to it in place; and the fracture of the bone is known because the limb is twisted and widely opened by force, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twist or pain in touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture, but it can have a twist, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with the hand, but apply medications that come here later, and then tighten it very subtly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes in an upward direction, and are the two disjointed parts, it is now necessary to put them back together evenly, so that the abscesses come one after another; and if hot abscesses come first, let them stay that way until the abscesses calm down; then place it evenly with gentle and precise movements, and know that the restoration of the bone is lighter than the restorations of those where pieces are missing; then tighten it as necessary afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken into two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or one of the smaller members, or at two joints, or at one joint and your hand, place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member align, all instruments used should be in their proper places, and take care through your work that the patient does not suffer any injury or pain; and adjust both pieces of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he will feel it well with his hand if it seems to him that it is not properly aligned: if the dressing is done neatly and not pulled too tightly, nor pressed as those who cause a hot abscess and contraction in the member by their own fault, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at rest, gently instruct the patient not to move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor turn, or in any other way, and ensure that the member is securely rested so as to feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet fully healed, and it is necessary to put it in a position where he feels no pain; and be careful that it is straightened properly, so that no distortion comes as it is restored, and the quality of the damaged member will depend on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken members are diverse in size and shape and strength.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Because there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones; it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloth; and for the larger ones, like the thigh or leg, it is necessary to wrap a wide and firm ligature around the entire member, embracing it equally from all sides so that there is no movement; then apply light bindings three times or four times, depending on the member, and tighten your hand slightly across the entire ligature, then go above the fracture and tighten less, allowing the fracture to move a little; and gradually soften the ligature bit by bit, pressing hard into the healthy part below until you have taken a good grip, then take another ligature and wrap it around again from the beginning over the fractured member; then return to the lower part of the fracture and tighten moderately, not too tightly or too loosely as we said in the first chapter above; then place soft bindings made of linen or cloth between the ligatures until they are even, then bind everything with a bandage on top, and then apply well-made splints above. If there is no abscess or swelling, do so.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, apply a soothing hot compress to it, which reduces the swelling, and leave it for several days; then tie your stars tightly, and make them half the width of a thin cane, or of wood used to make knives, or palm fronds, according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thread placed on the rupture be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and just as long as required for the member's size, whether small or large; then tighten the threads as you did in the first layer, and tie a fine thread over it, as in the first layer on the rupture; narrower at the end, but not too tight; and the thread should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the thread is thick, it's like the work of fools who make their bindings with twisted linen threads, and that's a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it's too fine, and it's not appropriate that there be less space between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is angry because of the pain from the stars after dislocating them in their joints, he should put compresses of linen or other soft cloth over them to avoid bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will then describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to dislocate all the stars of a member broken in the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is large, it is not appropriate to put stars inside until after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your judgment of the hotness of the abscess coming to the surface; and here is the ancient method of pastes to restore a dislocation, fracture, and twist: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, and make this preparation, not too clear or too thick, and use it; this is the common way of the paste that restores a break in various positions, especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for repairing breaks and dislocations and twists: take albac (almond) meal, ladan (resin), myrrh, and gum arabic, each in equal parts; add mirra (myrrh) and aloe in equal parts; add alech (spice) in nine parts; make it into a powder and mix with egg albumen; if the patient's body temperature is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and it heals broken bones quickly, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for twists: take mugat (a type of plant) and vismalve (a resin), each in ten parts; myrrh and aloe, each in seven parts; acaice (a herb) in six parts; Armenian balm in ten parts; grind well and mix with water or egg albumen; apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of splinting joints and realigning bones to their proper places, easing the pain that comes with it, and using bandages on the bone, and splints: take a new cloth, moisten it in hot oil, and wrap it around the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore, but they are good for easing hot abscesses and properly extracting bones that cause pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of splinting broken bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pawpaw leaves, crush them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of mending the broken bone and thereby alleviating the pain from the abscess's return.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the roots of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, and grain flour, each in equal parts; grind them, mix with wine, and apply to the affected member after heating it. Alternatively, mix with fresh coriander water or water alone, and use as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of mending the member when a hard abscess arises during restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and flaxseed, and fennel, and melilot, and chamomile, and flowers from violets, all in equal parts; grind and preserve with vinegar, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that to restore a broken member, one should not use anything but a mixture of wax and oil, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen suggests applying warm, dry substances to a broken member to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is effective for both injury and pain: take linen cloth and horse hair from men shorn, or feathers from an eye, or wool, and blend them equally, and make a paste and apply it and bind it firmly.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, after a little while, loosen it again and take care that the patient does not feel any pain or that the bone has not moved from its place; if pain appears along with itching, restlessness, or swelling, act quickly, loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately. Take a light cloth and a moist sponge from the sea, dip it in water, and gently lift the skin until the itching stops and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, and apply dry linen, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it up tightly, ensuring you are certain of the heat of the abscess. The inflammation of the affected limb will subside, and the pain will disappear; then continue with a delicate repetition of the process, using a little more plaster, but not too tightly as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed, red, painful and swollen, you have successfully treated it; but if it reappears, as you did at first, then you need to use plaster and binding.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the member does not heal as we have said, do not release it until after three or four or five or seven days; and under no circumstances leave it for twenty days, until the fracture is healed and the adjustment of the limb to its place is close; then tighten it more than before and fatten its flesh, as I have said above. And if you see that the healing is drying up more than necessary, immediately apply hot water, every time you release it, and let it rest for a short while; by this means cure the member, and avert the harmful consequences that come from the foolish practices of those who twist the limb in an incorrect manner: it is dangerous, and these practices are extremely harmful, and I do not see anything else but to leave it alone or do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fracturing bones, each with distinct shapes and causes. Some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, or when a bone is pierced all the way through, like a hatchet or axe; such fractures are known as 'hatchet wounds'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or, the sword may cut through the bone without piercing it completely, which is called 'absolute' fracture; and this type of injury can range from small to large wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a pulsation or swelling, or cutting from stones or from blows against stone, or from other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture, which approaches the bone tissue underneath or on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is healed in the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, this type of break is called "capillary"; and if the wound is caused by striking with stone or with a blow or similar things, and the piece of bone enters inward, and the edges are smooth like the craftsman's work on kettles; if it lodges between the bones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those with moist heads, such as an infant's head; and it occurs in all these ways of dislocation, that small pieces are separated as if they were broken; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of dislocations by pulling on them, and questioning at each point, and by corrupt flesh above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is recognized when, after uncovering the bone and rubbing it thoroughly, the dislocation gap opens up.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be wary of accidents with the patient, and if you notice any harmful accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, dilation, numbness, fever, sudden heat or redness, or other similar symptoms in various combinations, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any dangerous accidents and hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the frost comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon, if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it happens that you hasten to remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone is corrupted, then come the complications that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone extends to the tissue covering the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part in this way: and you pierce the patient's head with pain, and expose the bone in every way possible, and smooth the wound surface as much as you can, and if blood oozes upon exposing the bone, or an abscess forms, you should seek help from those who know, and fill the wound with moist, rose-scented cloth; and rest the wound until the abscess is healed, and be assured of no further bleeding. Then, begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you cut through the narrowest part first, and this is its shape...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I use another treatment even greater than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many different shapes, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron indelible; and make them lightly, without damaging the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is necessary that you pierce it around, so as to administer cuts with measure, not allowing the point to go beyond the bone's soft part, and there must be a margin or a circle on top of the point, preventing it from penetrating further into the bone; and you need several of them, so that each one reaches its place according to the bone's thickness, ensuring measures for all bones; and this is the form of the three types of cuts:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to percé the bone without breaking it is that you apply pressure on the bone and return your hand to its original position as long as you know the bone is pierced; then place the pressure elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut with incisions the space between the cracks of the bone, and do so as delicately as possible, lightly, as we have said, while you still hold the bone in your hand or with any tool you have like tongs or pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain nor the soft tissue.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you remove the tension remaining from the bone to all other tools resembling an incision instrument, but it should be more tense and subtler than the other incision instruments; and if nothing remains of the small bones or scales, gently remove them with the appropriate tool; then dress the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen says, which is safer; it is very powerful, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either where the fracture is open, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place the tip of this curved scalpel beneath it, whose shape is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut through any part, and it is the acute side in the second rib, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike slightly with a small hammer, so that you gently chip away the bone all around, and take great care of the tissue beneath; if it is detached from the bone, gently lift it, because otherwise it will be cut badly, and with much pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and shave off the scales with a delicate razor, having various quantities of it at hand, in order to make each one suitable for its place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great difficulties and then even more subtle ones, do not cease from this task until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to make adjustments according to their location; and this is a matter that is not easily answered for one who has dedicated his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if it pleases him to reveal itself, you must press the linen drape according to the size of the wound, soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double drape, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first drape; do this as gently as possible so as not to damage the syphilis, then apply a second bandage, without straining it so that it only covers the wound; leave it for a day or two until the abscess subsides, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, meal flour, incense powder, aristology, and similar substances; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and keep applying unprescribed medicines without burning; ensure that the wound remains clean, do not leave behind any treatment, or let it form boils, for when they gather on the flesh of the head, they corrode and destroy, causing great harm to the patient, since putting anything sharp on the syphilis causes damage.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes not from the medicine that has been placed there, but that its virtue is in question, then you should mix a part of honey with three parts of rose oil and a drape of glue, and apply it to the wound; then cure it in the manner of cures that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You know that the two parts of the bone above are never broken, either together or separately, for they are two bones; and this one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but only bends or twists, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you insert your little finger or a thin tool between the joints, and place the fracture correctly in your index finger, and hold it by force, until the joint returns to its natural position; do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain due to your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the joint, and the fingers cannot return to their place, then it is necessary that you place it equally at the head of a slightly thicker thread.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is from both parts, do the same thing, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or fifth day, when the abscess has subsided, then place thin linen strips at the head of the joint, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or turn to another part, if it is broken; and make sure the splints are so thick that they fill the openings of the wounds.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is complete unless the splints are soaked in butter and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think this is good, but it is necessary that they be soaked in a mixture of egg and flour powder; then leave the splints, as long as the bones are hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never burn the patient with goose feathers in place of others, and if it pricks around the wound, and holds the break, and blows the pain among; or do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses appear at the new wound while you are treating it, apply a plaster or moist cotton in rose oil, or in a poultice of eagle's fat.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess forms, apply a plaster made of sesame flour and incense powder, confited with egg yolk, then place light bandages on it without binding the neig; and if the break in the neig is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then clean the wound with hot oil and charcoals, and treat it with plasters and poultices as needed until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is ruptured and there is no external wound, and the fracture is not severe enough to cause two pieces to be separated, but it is slightly displaced, then if you gently know how to recognize it, it can be realigned.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side of the jaw, you should insert your index finger of the left hand into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, press the fracture gently from inside using your index finger of the right hand, and with the other hand pull it slightly outward, making them both equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is severe in two places, it is necessary that you administer an extension to both parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth causes a fracture, or if it is a break resulting from tension with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place cerate on the broken jaw and cover it with two layers of cloth; put the cloth under a large, well-made star or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and secure it as best you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you notice that the shape changes on the third day, then readjust it; apply plaster next, mixing fine powder with enough egg or sesame flour after removing the cerate, and place a thin layer of plaster, letting it harden without disturbing the patient's condition, as long as it remains healthy. It often heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess forms, it is necessary to treat it as we have often said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, do not attempt to extract any pieces of bone that are still intact; use delicate tools for this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, expand it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after you have extracted all these pieces and it does not delay, clean the wound if it is wide, and cover it with suitable bandages to promote healing.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times near the shoulder, and the fracture is in three manners: it may be broken and displaced into two parts, with fragments, and is easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with an accompanying wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And for the work when there is no wound accompanying the fracture, you need two assistants: one holds the injured part that is broken with the forceps; the other extends the collar towards the affected area; then equalize the fracture at both your hands, so that the shape is as it should be and shows neither bulge nor depression.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round spear of cloth or wool under the shoulder of the patient, as thick as necessary; stretch and relax the arm, hold the spear with your hand, and align the fracture properly, as is appropriate.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the arm out due to its attachment, since it comes off completely, then the patient should lie on their side with the injured arm under their body, and have someone press down on the shoulder above, until the bone of the arm is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel any debris, it's fine to cut; pull out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined together in any way, use this instrument under the arm to prevent further harm.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it should look like a spoon, and is not missing, and is as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the scope of the work; and it has two parts, as you can see, one wider, the other narrower, just like the wound's edge that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, if you cut the wound, and if the incision is small, then you doubt a hot abscess, if you cover the wound with cloth or bandages, according to its amount.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses occur, then moisten the cloth with rose oil and wool and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is pierced or cut, is to place the plaster of fine, ground powder and egg white upon it, and put light bandages over, and insert a spike under the armpit if necessary; then take a very wide, three-finger-breadth strip of cloth, and place the double bandage over the bandages and plaster; next, take a thin, three-inch-wide and long stele, and wrap it around the cloth so that the edge of the cloth is hanging down; and place the stele on the fracture, and turn the cloth back over the shoulder, and under the healthy armpit and the afflicted one; rearrange each part, and when you see that the plaster holds well to the fractured bone, and clearly see that the stele does not move upon the broken bone, reward it with attention each day, and when the ties loosen, tighten them again; and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit to raise the dislocated part higher; lighten the fracture's strain by aligning the shoulder, or fasten the arm to the chest, and do not take it off for twenty days unless bad accidents occur; then repeat the plastering if necessary, tighten it, and leave it thus until it is healed; and it will be healed in no more than twenty-eight days, and sometimes less for men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is dislocated far or deeply, it will not remain in place except by touch; if you put it back according to the shape of the dislocation and restore it to its natural state in every way possible, then sprinkle some fine, mild powder on the joint and apply light bandages, and cover with a double cloth. Then place a wide and thin steel plate, slightly larger than the shoulder, and so that it rests against all parts of the shoulder; use strips of linen for this, so that the steel plate is cut equally. And then tighten it firmly with a strong bandage so that the steel plate does not move from its place, and check it each day. Whenever it loosens, tighten it again and return the steel plate to its correct position if it has moved, and have the patient lie on his side. The shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days, and when this number of days is reached, untie it and be sure, for it is not a bone that can be put back easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of bone sticks out and does not go inside the wound, it is necessary to do as we have said in the calming of the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the rupture of the worst
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The skin is never broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; but it often breaks at the extreme.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it recedes inside and causes the patient great pain, and weakness, and sometimes bleeds, and opens up the wound in the broken bone, and it feels much better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and puts a cushion between his shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs to both hands, and carefully adjusts it in all ways so that the bone figure is as it should be; then apply plasters and compresses over the gentle salt star or other light bandage, and wrap it in a cloth, binding it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and tighten the bandage around the back, adjusting it properly, and check the patient every hour, and if it softens, tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened, due to corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, act quickly, loosen it, remove the plaster, and address the cure that has come about; then apply the plaster again, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in the upper back and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are broken; and this causes great pain to the patient.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put it back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, tightening it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inside, then the patient feels very great pain and stabbing, as if from crying, because the bone pierces the skin; also with hands, and sometimes he coughs and vomits a lot of blood, which is a great illness, and old doctors put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to expel the fracture from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not pretend that hot poultices will not come if they have not already arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes back, as healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that none of you should place suction cups on the limb for bloodletting, as it seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction cup might draw away the excess fluids from the limb due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of you should cover the limb with moist wool and hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to even out the space around, then apply treatment for pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear through the bone where the fracture is, then doubt arises in the patient, and it is necessary to cut into the broken rib cage, and place an instrument to hold it in place; and then the bone must be cut, and pulled gently, and then sew together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with bandages until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses appear, place moistened linen cloths soaked in rose oil on the affected area and lay the patient down; treat while the abscess is present, keeping them elevated on the side where it is located, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Of the dislocation of the collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No dislocation occurs in the collarbone bone, and rarely if it rains; also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone and you want to know if they will recover, be on the lookout for their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and unable to move or stretch them; if you can push an needle through without pain, then there is little hope.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	You know that it is deadly in many ways; if the limbs remain motionless and there is no pain when they are moved slightly, then know that the joint of the bone is intact and the patient will recover, if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, be vigilant if the legs are weakened, and if there are accidents in the hands, and on the back, excessive sweating and ejection without will; and when it is recalled to its belly, then excessive ejection without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is recalled to its back and wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly: do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that if there is a hot abscess, you apply warm rose oil or egg yolk oil to it until it is calmed; then put a comforting and drying plaster on it and secure it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, it should be covered with a bandage; then the bone is reduced, and the two edges of the wound are sewn together if it is large, then dressed with ointment and bound tightly until it heals; and if the fragment of the bone is broken off, which is called the "fragment of the joint," you press your empty hand against it on one side, and place it level with the other hand, then apply the plaster and the splint, as needed; then tighten it, and if there are any dislocated bones, reduce them, and pull out, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the fracture of the bone of the shoulder blade
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone of the shoulder blade is fractured, and there is not even a slight reduction in pain at the site, it causes great pain, swelling, and inflammation where the fracture occurs.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over the fracture site, ensuring you understand where the fracture is and its shape; if the fracture is only at the top, then equalize the fracture until it returns to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is very long, it bends inward, so make the patient lie on his belly until the restoration of that fracture becomes visible.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place a splint over it, then put a wooden or iron rod on top and hold the fracture steady so that it does not move, and use the hand under the ribs to make them even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears and is not touched, as long as the abscess remains calm, apply what we have mentioned above; then return to restoration, tightening it as appropriate, unless there is some adverse event; this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The "ajutoire" refers to the joint between the collarbone and the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it must be restored using one of two methods: one involves taking a thick, sturdy strip, shaped as follows...
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And hold the two pieces of the shoulder together and bend them upwards, and watch over the patient lying down; then break one of his arms on the thigh until it reaches the socket, and place a wooden splint in between, then bend it onto any heavy object or have the assistant pull it downward; then adjust the braces equally with both hands until the fracture returns to its proper place.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is to lay the patient on his back and tie one hand to his neck, then instruct the assistants to have one apply pressure over the fracture at the level of the hands, while the other stretches all the ligaments, extending them as far as possible.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too painful, hold the broken piece firmly, and on the break, stretch each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the shoulder joint, it is necessary to put a moderate tie below the acromion and another towards the throat, below the break; and likewise, if the break is on the side of the throat, it is advisable to place a light tie without effort, as long as the break remains level on the bone, then set the dislocation correctly and tighten it gently without causing complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the abscess opens on its own, do not touch it for seven days, and place a moist cloth with rose oil on the opening until the abscess is calmed; then apply pressure, and know that you should put a splint over the fracture, then bring the arm up to the aid, and place your hand on the shoulder or under the breast; and cover it with a cloth, and apply pressure to the aid and the arm, so that the arm is in a straight position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
